Roosevelt Approves Silver Agreement World Silver Prices Stabilize 61

Promulgates Proclamation to Mint Silver Coins

Far East Trade Can Increase Greatly

London Observers Not Optimistic

(Washington) The US President today approved the London Silver Agreement concluded at the World Economic Conference this autumn, and approved people to send newly mined silver to mint silver coins.

According to the Silver Agreement, the US government will purchase 24 million ounces of domestically mined silver annually at a price of 64.5 cents per ounce over the next four years. It is generally believed that the President's approval is aimed at stabilizing the government's silver plan, hoping to gain the support of silver-state congressmen for the government's monetary policy, divide the forces of inflationists, and avoid an inflationary currency war in Congress.

Regarding the minting of silver coins, the President's proclamation stated that, in accordance with the Congressional bill, silver mined in the country and its territories may be sent to the mint for minting silver coins. However, half of the silver sent to the mint must be turned over to the government, collected by the national treasury, and used as seigniorage and handling fees. The remaining half, after being minted into silver coins, will be returned to the original owner. It also stated that, in order to help stabilize domestic prices and protect foreign trade from the adverse effects of foreign currency devaluation, it is now necessary to raise and stabilize silver prices.

The amount of silver that the US government intends to purchase annually is roughly equal to the total amount of silver mined domestically last year, and its value is half of the legal price in the mint. Therefore, those who want to send silver for minting silver coins must turn over half to the government.

It is now believed that the President's move will appease the appeals of silver-producing states, dispose of the surplus silver on the market, and at the same time enhance the economic position of the United States in the Far East. Senator Pittman, who was the initiator of negotiating the Silver Agreement at the London Conference, was very pleased to hear the news of the approval today, saying that the agreement is expected to raise world silver prices and increase the purchasing power of the Far East by 50%.

According to the Silver Agreement, India, China, and Spain, as the largest silver-holding countries, guarantee not to dump large amounts of silver abroad within four years. The United States, Mexico, Peru, Australia, and Canada, as the largest silver-producing countries, have agreed to limit production and purchase a portion of their production for minting coins or currency reserves. It is also stipulated that if this agreement has not been fully approved by April 1 of next year, silver-holding countries may no longer be bound, while silver-producing countries will still be bound. (National News Agency dispatch from the 21st)

Roosevelt's Proclamation 62

Pursuant to the May Congressional Act

President has the Power to Mint Gold and Silver Coins

(Washington) President Roosevelt's proclamation regarding the minting of silver coins; the original text is as follows:

Whereas, Section 2 of Chapter 43 of the Congressional Act passed on May 12, 1933, authorizes the President to prescribe the weight of gold coins that are nine-tenths fine and the weight of silver coins that are nine-tenths fine, in such quantities as the President, after investigation, deems necessary to stabilize domestic commodity prices or protect the currency; the President has the authority to mint an unlimited amount of gold and silver coins at the determined ratio;

And whereas, based on my investigation, I believe that in assisting the stabilization of domestic prices and in adhering to the policies and procedures currently implemented and approved by Congress, it is necessary to raise and stabilize the price of silver in order to protect our foreign trade from the adverse effects of debased foreign currencies;

And whereas, the resolution proposed by the U.S. delegation was adopted by the representatives of sixty-six nations at the World Economic Conference on July 27, 1933, stipulating that each government abandon the policy and practice of melting or reducing silver coins, stipulating that low-value silver certificates should be replaced with silver coins, and stipulating that no legislation should be enacted that could depress the price of silver;

And whereas, the supplementary agreements concluded between the silver-using countries of China, India, Spain, and the silver-producing countries of Australia, Canada, Mexico, Peru, and the United States, state that China agrees not to melt or reduce silver coins for the purpose of selling its silver, India agrees not to sell more than 35 million ounces of its silver annually for four years starting from January 1, 1934, and Spain also agrees not to sell more than 5 million ounces of its silver annually during the same period; India and Spain also agree to abide by the resolutions passed by the World Economic Conference thereafter;

Considering the aforementioned restrictions, the governments of the five silver-producing countries agree to purchase a certain amount of silver from their respective domestic mines; the amount of silver purchased by the silver-producing countries shall be 35 million ounces annually, for a period of four years starting from January 1, 1934; the silver thus acquired shall be retained by the four countries for four years for the purpose of minting coins or as currency reserves, and shall not be sold on the market within the four years; and it is understood that the United States, within this total amount of 35 million ounces, will annually purchase at least 24,421,410 ounces of silver produced in its own country for a period of four years;

Now, therefore, feeling that cooperation with other governments is appropriate, and that raising and stabilizing domestic prices, increasing the purchasing power of the people of silver-using countries, protecting our foreign commerce from the adverse effects of debased foreign currencies, and implementing the understanding reached among the sixty-six nations in the aforementioned resolution are also necessary, I, Franklin D. Roosevelt, President of the United States, by virtue of the authority vested in me by the Act of Congress and other legislation aimed at national recovery, and by virtue of other powers vested in the President, do hereby proclaim and direct the mints of the United States to receive silver bullion for the purpose of minting standard silver dollars, provided that the mint shall, in accordance with regulations prescribed by the Secretary of the Treasury, ascertain that the silver so received is derived from mines in the United States or its territories from the date of this proclamation;

The director of the mint, with the voluntary consent of the original owner, shall deduct fifty percent of the silver received as seigniorage and for the costs to the U.S. government of minting and transporting the silver coins; the remaining fifty percent shall be minted into standard silver dollars and delivered in full to the original owner;

The fifty percent of silver retained shall be held by the Treasury Department and shall not be sold before the end of December 1937, except for the purpose of minting United States silver coins;

The Secretary of the Treasury is authorized to formulate regulations to implement this proclamation; such regulations shall contain the terms and conditions previously established under the Act of Congress of April 23, known as the Pittman Act, with such modifications as may be necessary to determine the method of verifying that the silver originates from mines in the United States or its territories after the date of this proclamation;

This proclamation shall remain in effect until December 31, 1937, unless repealed or amended by an Act of Congress or by a subsequent proclamation. (Reuter's dispatch on the 21st)

Christmas 63

American Commerce Improves

British Monarch to Broadcast Address

(London) On Christmas Day afternoon, the British monarch will deliver a short address, broadcast via radio to all peoples of the British Empire. In addition, a separate broadcast program is planned, in which the current situation in London and other parts of the mother country will be communicated to all parts of the Empire. Furthermore, there will be a speech from the bottom of a very deep mine in Wales, and the keeper of the Trevose Head Lighthouse in Northumberland will also speak. (Reuter's dispatch on the 22nd)

(New York) Residents of major American cities have recently been happily purchasing gifts in preparation for the Christmas holiday. According to official surveys, commerce has gradually shown signs of improvement. (Reuter's dispatch on the 21st)

Promoting Recovery Plan 64

Pittman Expresses Delight

(Washington) Senator Pittman believes that President Roosevelt's proclamation can greatly increase U.S. export trade and promote the stabilization of the world silver price at 64.5 cents per ounce. Pittman is very pleased and is confident that Canada, Australia, Mexico, and Peru will take similar actions. With the increase in the price of silver, the exchange rates and purchasing power of these countries will also increase accordingly. From then on, commodity prices can rise, and the recovery and restoration of normalcy in the United States can be accelerated. (Reuter's dispatch on the 21st)

(Washington) After President Roosevelt held a cabinet meeting and consulted with Morgenthau and Cummings, he issued a proclamation on the minting of silver coins, referring to the Thomas Amendment authorizing the President to change the gold and silver content of the dollar, and stated that after his own investigation, he felt that it was necessary to raise and stabilize the price of silver in order to raise and stabilize domestic commodity prices, increase the purchasing power of silver-using countries, and protect American foreign trade from the adverse effects of the devaluation of foreign currencies. This proclamation will be effective until the end of 1937 unless repealed or amended in the future. The President also mentioned India's ratification of the London Silver Agreement and said that he was aware that other countries would take similar actions, and he believed that complying with this agreement would stabilize the price of silver and subject it to the laws of supply and demand. (Reuter's dispatch on the 21st)

Global Impact 65

London's Observation Is Not Optimistic

(London) London, New York, and Bombay all expect that President Roosevelt's actions may not have much impact on the world silver price. According to news from Bombay, there is replenishment of short positions, but the general market conditions there are now awaiting London's attitude. Wall Street in New York has doubts about the impact on world trade, believing that China wants cheap silver in order to revitalize its export trade. If the price of silver soars, China, with its large silver reserves, will inevitably sell it, which will depress the London silver price. London financial circles say that the United States' purchase of gold has not been able to control world prices, so this time the U.S. silver policy may encounter the same fate. When the silver-using and silver-producing countries announced their agreement to restrict the sale of silver at the World Economic Conference, the price of silver only rose slightly, but soon rebounded, so the situation in the future should be the same. It is found that American speculators have about 150 million ounces of silver in stock, eager to sell it off. Although last year's silver production was only 160 million ounces, a decrease of 80 million ounces compared to the average of the past ten years, the world's accumulated silver reserves are still very large. Public opinion generally believes that only the recovery of world trade can permanently raise the price of silver, and the first key to achieving this goal is for China, the largest silver-using country, to solve its problems of exorbitant taxes, warlords, and redundant troops. If this can be implemented, it can restore the prosperity of its internal economy. (Reuter's dispatch on the 22nd)

(London) Major brokers here expect the price of silver to rise by 0.25 to 0.5 pence today. Although President Roosevelt's silver decision has caused a reaction in the market here, the public is not optimistic about the effectiveness of stabilization in the near future. It is generally recognized that speculative demand will soon arise, but the current situation is very unstable, fearing that China's silver reserves will be sold off due to high prices. Moreover, the United States' silver production only accounts for one-sixth of the world's total production. The amount of silver that India is allowed to export is set at 35 million ounces, which is far more than its recent total exports. Therefore, the public expects that the impact of President Roosevelt's decision will not be very significant or lasting. (Reuter's dispatch on the 22nd)

(London) After news of the U.S. approval of the silver agreement arrived in England, the major London market rose 0.5 pence today, with spot prices rising from 18.5625 pence per ounce to 19.0625 pence, and forward prices for delivery in two months rising from 18.5625 pence to 19.125 pence. (National Telegraph on the 22nd)

Seattle Tonight, the silver market exchange here has been very active in buying silver, with some unable to purchase it. The price of silver has risen by three cents per ounce, which is the maximum daily fluctuation allowed in Washington State. (National Telegraph on the 21st)

(New York) The U.S. President's approval of the silver agreement and the publication of a statement on the silver plan came as a surprise to everyone on Wall Street. Silver immediately rose by 215 points (i.e., 2.15 cents), stocks rose by 1 to 10 points, cotton rose by one dollar, and grain rose by five cents. Silver opened up by 200 points. By 10:30, the January price had increased from 45.20 cents to 45.30 cents, and the March price was 45.5 cents. (National Telegraph on the 22nd)

Cuba Also Mints Silver Coins 66

Havana The Cuban government is now considering minting an additional 20 million silver pesos to be stored in the national treasury as reserves for issuing silver certificates to alleviate financial difficulties. It is reported that Finance Minister Despaigne is in favor of this measure and has drafted an order for President San Martín to consider. If San Martín agrees, he will sign it into effect. It is rumored that a Cuban bank can lend funds to purchase silver and mint coins. It is said that the government can issue silver certificates to cover the most urgent government expenses and debts. In the future, Cuban taxpayers will be able to pay 70% of their taxes in silver certificates. If this plan becomes a reality, there will be a total of 38 million silver pesos in Cuba. (National Telegraph on the 21st)

Simon Arrives in Paris, Anglo-French Talks Begin 67

British Policy Remains Ambiguous

Mediator Position Makes It Difficult

(Paris) Anglo-French disarmament talks began this morning at the Foreign Ministry, but the critical moment will be in the afternoon, as British Foreign Secretary Simon, British Ambassador Tyrrell, French Premier Chautemps, and French Foreign Minister Bonnet will all be present in the afternoon. According to the opinion of French observers, the only possible result is the clarification of French policy. As for British policy, it will remain ambiguous, as Britain's position as a mediator is indeed very difficult. (Reuter's dispatch on the 22nd)

Simon Announces British Policy to the House of Commons 68

Multilateral Convention Better Than Unilateral Declaration

League of Nations Should Not Be Allowed to Collapse

(London) Today, Foreign Secretary Simon attended the House of Commons to report on the major trends in international diplomacy. The main points were German Chancellor Hitler's recent proposal to sign non-aggression treaties with neighboring countries, and Britain's efforts to facilitate an agreement between Germany and France. Simon first stated that negotiations parallel and auxiliary to the Disarmament Conference are already underway in various European capitals, so the disarmament issue has not stopped for a moment. He then said that Hitler has repeatedly issued declarations in favor of cooperation between Germany and France, and that the British government has always been extremely concerned about this matter, but at the same time has made it clear that its position is that of an investigator and is not affiliated with any recommendations. Furthermore, the British government has also solemnly stated that it has not shunned the various obligations borne by members of the League of Nations, and that the non-aggression treaty now proposed should also be bounded by these obligations. Simon then described the purpose of his upcoming travels abroad, saying that he would take the opportunity to discuss Germany's proposal with French Foreign Minister Bonnet, as close cooperation between Germany and France is the most important issue today. According to Simon's opinion, he believes that a common agreement between international organizations is better than mutual treaties between two countries, and the League of Nations should not be allowed to collapse but should be allowed to progress slowly. He does not have extreme expectations for the future, but he feels that there is now a widespread exchange of views between governments, so he believes that when the first meeting is convened after Christmas, countries will definitely have a more definitive decision on British policy. At present, because Germany has already agreed to accept the joint management of armaments, with the condition that the armaments of other countries must be subject to the same joint management, the greatest goal in the future will be to make Japan and other countries accept the same conditions. Therefore, in Simon's personal opinion, the final result of this negotiation must not be satisfied with a declaration by one party alone, but must have a convention, signed jointly by all countries, in order to have a great effect. (National Telegraph on the 22nd)

Mussolini's Ambition to Rebuild the Roman Empire 69

Italian Influence Extends Eastward

Will Conflict Head-on with Japanese Policy

Rome At the opening ceremony of the Asian Students' Congress here this morning, there was a surge of support for the connection between Italy and the East. The opening ceremony of the Congress was held in the Hall of Mars, the Caesar Augustus Hall in Rome. The venue was decorated with flags and ribbons, and 600 Asian students attended, of whom about 500 were students at major European universities, and about 100 were students at Italian universities. There were many teachers and religious students, as well as Eastern students wearing headscarves, and female students wearing national costumes, which attracted particular attention. Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, accompanied by Fascist Party Secretary Starace and Undersecretary of Foreign Affairs Suvich, arrived at 11:45 a.m. As he entered the venue, the crowd cheered. Minister of Education Ercole, Director of the Oriental Institute and former Minister of Education Santi, Professor Mabbikate, and Count Ciano, Director of the Information Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and former Minister to China, greeted him at the door. Mussolini then took the stage to deliver a speech, first in Italian and then in English, saying in essence that the ancient Roman Empire, based on the Mediterranean coast, united the East and the West, which was of utmost importance in world history. At that time, Western countries and Syria, Egypt, and Persia were all colonies of the Roman Empire. Rome and these countries knew each other and benefited greatly. This kind of East-West unity is the foundation of our entire history. Today's European civilization originated from this. Now, if we want to avoid extinction, we must make it universal throughout the world. (Havas dispatch on the 22nd)

Rome For some time, Far Eastern affairs have occupied a particularly important position in Italian newspapers. The "Middle East and Far East Institute" was established today, and the Asian University Students' Association took the opportunity to hold a gathering. The public regards this as the most important event, and all believe that this is enough to represent the revival of "ancient Rome and Italy and Latin." The Fascist University Student Group issued a declaration to the Asian students, stating that "Rome is a city that will last forever, and its history is full of glory. Today, the reason for hosting Asian representatives is to complete a new mission, which is to unite the world as one family, and not just confine it to one corner of Europe." The fact that Rome is hosting Asian university students is especially meaningful at a time when Italian newspapers continue to oppose Japanese imperialism. Italian newspapers do not hide their fear of Japanese business policies. "Il Popolo d'Italia" stated that Japan's dumping policies in Australia, India, Africa, and Europe are indeed a very serious sign. When the newspaper published this kind of opinion, the Chinese military observation delegation, led by Yang Jie, President of the Army University, was traveling in various parts of Italy and visiting the demonstrations of assault vehicles and trailers. It is said that in the early spring of this year, chemical factories in northern Italy, especially in Milan, which have equipment for manufacturing explosives and suffocating gases, purchased a large number of raw materials and stepped up their work. It is currently rumored that this manufacturing is for a certain country in the Far East. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

France's Aviation Aims to Dominate Europe and Asia 70

Largest and Fastest Airplane Departs

(Paris) The French-made L'Emeraude, the largest and fastest passenger airplane, which aims to dominate the air routes of Europe and Asia, departed from Paris–Le Bourget Airport yesterday, carrying passengers and mail to Mandalay, Burma, and Annam, and is scheduled to arrive in Saigon in four days. French Airlines General Manager Guillaumet personally went to the airport to see it off. The aircraft is a monoplane that can carry twelve passengers and is equipped with three engines. If this trip is successful, it will join the regular flights between Paris and Saigon. It is reported that it will stop in Marseille to collect mail and will land in Mandalay, Burma, because several passengers are disembarking. (National Telegraph on the 22nd)

Poland Adopts Sun Yat-sen's Political Tutelage 71

Countries Worldwide Inclined to Abolish Parliaments

Warsaw Today, the Polish Parliament discussed the new constitution and cited Sun Yat-sen's famous saying that all citizens can be trained to be good citizens, but only a few can exercise governing power, as proof that in the future, the election of senators will be determined only by work performance, and the universal suffrage system will be abolished. At the same time, efforts will be made to prevent the parliament from becoming a purely debating body, because the parliament has members from 35 different political parties, and debates will inevitably be disorderly. Moreover, some political parties lack a solid foundation. In order to promote the improvement of Polish politics, the political tutelage method planned by Sun Yat-sen will be adopted. Other democratic countries also have the same tendency, because many inexperienced democratic groups can only cause factional disputes and hinder the development of government affairs when handling national affairs. Austria decided to exercise supervisory power over the parliament in September last year. The power of the Italian House of Representatives has long been stripped away, and it will soon be dissolved and replaced by the Fascist Grand Council and the National Professional Associations. However, in the recent elections in Spain, 44 political parties competed, and there were 7,000 candidates. Romania had 4,000 candidates, representing 22 political parties. It is still difficult to predict the outcome of Spain and Romania, but it is rumored that there is a movement in Romania against the parliament, believing that the parliament is enough to hinder the king's intention to represent the people's will. Therefore, at present, the rulers of various countries, such as Japan, believe that they can represent the people and that the corruption of the parliamentary system is enough to hinder the true spirit of democracy. (Reuter's dispatch on the 22nd)

Soviet Russia Trains Women Soldiers 72

(Moscow) The National Women's Association announced that it will provide special training to women who want to serve in the military and raise funds to cover the expenses. (National Telegraph on the 21st)

Hirota's Cultural Diplomacy 73

(Tokyo) In order to introduce Japanese culture overseas, Foreign Minister Hirota planned to establish an International Cultural Bureau, but its budget failed to pass the budget cabinet meeting. The Foreign Minister then discussed with representatives from the private sector to establish a cultural organization to replace the Cultural Bureau. As a result, a joint government-private international cultural promotion initiators' meeting was convened on the afternoon of the 21st. From the private sector, well-known figures such as Tokugawa Yorisada, Count Kabayama, Count Kuroda, Viscount Okabe, Baron Gō Seinosuke, Baron Ōkura, Kushida, Fukui, Kodama, and Asaki attended. First, the Foreign Minister explained the purpose of establishing the Cultural Promotion Association and sought everyone's approval for this move. Baron Gō Seinosuke represented everyone in expressing their strong support. After discussion, it was decided that the Foreign Minister would appoint a special committee to carry out preparations. Of the budget of one million yen, 200,000 yen would be paid by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the rest would be raised through donations from various sources. (Domei News Agency dispatch on the 22nd)

French Crack Down on Espionage Agency Spying for Soviet Russia 74

Police Consider It the Most Shocking Incident Since the War

Those Arrested Include Men and Women from Russia, France, and America

A Professor Fluent in 68 Languages

(Paris) The French arrest of 18 spies is considered by the police to be the most important espionage case in French history since the war. Those arrested include Russians, French, Romanians, Americans, Canadians, and Yugoslavians. It is reported that these people are dedicated to serving Soviet Russia, but they also spy for the governments of several other countries. The most prominent figures among those arrested are a professor who is fluent in 68 languages and a highly educated Russian woman. (Reuter's dispatch on the 21st)

(Paris) After a thorough investigation of the recent espionage case uncovered here, the police discovered another case. Of the ten spies arrested, eight are foreigners, and one named Martin is a member of the French Naval Ministry's code section. Martin, who is fluent in several languages, was bribed along with a Russian named Steele by a certain country to undertake the task of reorganizing espionage affairs in Finland. Two other female spies, Sulle and Van Lan, cooperated with him. The other spies are responsible for investigating the military organization of France in the East and Southeast. The police recently found a large number of documents in the residence of Steele's wife in the suburbs, all of which are related to the case of reorganizing espionage affairs in Finland. (Havas dispatch on the 21st)

Franco-German Trade Negotiations Break Down 75

Japanese and Puppet Troops Still Have Not Withdrawn from Chahar 80

Pingfang Says Reports of Japanese Troops Returning to Rehe Are Inaccurate

Chahar Provincial Government Orders All Troops to Maintain Strict Vigilance

Zhangjiakou Correspondence The westward invasion of Rehe by Japanese and puppet troops and the tension in eastern Chahar, as well as Tang Yulin's return to the Chahar Provincial Government, have all been noticed by the people of the country. The situation is described below:

The Situation in Eastern Chahar Remains Tense 81

Approximately three to four thousand Japanese and puppet troops are stationed in the Rehe-Fengning area, equipped with several cannons and airplanes. On the 11th and 12th of the month, a unit of over a thousand troops, under the guise of suppressing bandits, suddenly advanced westward, reaching Xinyuan County on the Chahar border. Xinyuan County was originally the second and fourth districts of Guyuan, but due to its distance from the county seat, a separate county government was established at Xifengzhai. On the morning of the 13th, the Japanese and puppet troops arrived near Xifengzhai and immediately engaged with the garrison forces of the county, led by Ma Jinliang and Huang Shouzhong. These two units were originally mixed troops, lacking training, and the suddenness of the attack caused them considerable losses. They retreated slightly. Zhang Shusheng, the special commissioner of Xinyuan, then led his team to Longmensuo to set up defenses. After entering Xifengzhai, the Japanese and puppet troops then advanced to Sunjiaying, twelve li from Longmensuo, but did not continue to advance. They posted notices along the way, claiming that the advance was to suppress bandits, and also urged the people to repair roads. On the 16th and 17th, news came from the front that most of the Japanese and puppet troops had withdrawn, but in fact, the Japanese and puppet troops did not move backward, and the situation remained tense. On the 20th, the provincial government received a report and instructed all units in eastern Chahar to pay close attention to defense and to reorganize defenses to prevent oversights. In addition to Guyuan, which is still defended by Zhang Yunrong, the troops of Liu Guitang in Chicheng will be temporarily transferred to □□, and other strong troops will be sent to take over the defense. Song Zheyuan also plans to personally inspect eastern Chahar. According to a responsible person in Chahar Province, who spoke to reporters on the 19th, the Japanese and puppet troops' westward invasion, though under the guise of suppressing bandits and clearing the border, was actually waiting for an opportunity and had ulterior motives. Chahar Province cannot ignore this. Also, at the beginning of the battle at Xifengzhai, it was widely rumored that the Japanese army was invading eastern Chahar in three routes: the northern route attacking Guyuan from Duolun, the central route probing Dushikou from Dage in Rehe, and the southern route attacking Chicheng from Heihe. The garrison troops of Liu Guitang in Chicheng, because the Chicheng area was difficult to control, once moved their headquarters to Yangtianbao, southeast of the county. When they heard that the battle had stopped, they led their troops back into the city to garrison.

Mixed Troops Undergoing Reorganization 82

Since the incident, the troops in Chahar Province have been complex and varied. After Song Zheyuan returned to Chahar, he actively reorganized them and personally went to various places to review and address the troops. Progress has been made so far, but some units still need thorough reorganization. For example, the Huang Shouzhong unit stationed near Xifengzhai in eastern Chahar was originally a habitual bandit in the Chahar-Rehe border area. After being incorporated, they became a detachment commander, but kidnapping and extortion continued as before. As for the □□□ and other units, their relationship with the Japanese and puppet troops is still entangled. Representatives come to the provincial capital from time to time, either requesting funds or asking for more equipment. The recent incident in eastern Chahar has given these people an opportunity to threaten. Song Zheyuan recently told a representative of a certain unit, "I have three ways of treating the various units: first, if they train hard according to the methods of training troops, I will treat them well; second, if they are neither close nor distant and just perfunctorily go through the motions, I will also treat them perfunctorily; third, if they act like bandits, I will treat them like bandits." These words, both gentle and stern, serve as a warning.

Tang Yulin's Troops Reorganized 83

Tang Yulin, the former chairman of Rehe, who once held great power and influence, has, since losing his province, been impoverished and forced to the border of Rehe. Recently, he arrived in Chahar, transferred his troops to Chahar Province, and went to Zhangjiakou alone. Song Zheyuan appointed him as the chief advisor of the 29th Army, and he has taken office. Tang now lives in the house of the cattle and sheep tax investigation office in Xiabao, Zhangjiakou, with more than twenty guards and more than twenty stable servants. He has nothing to do every day except for social engagements. His son, Tang Zuo, and others are in Tianjin and send people to Zhangjiakou from time to time to inquire. Tang Yulin recently intended to leave Zhangjiakou and sent someone to see Song Zheyuan to discuss it. Song asked him to rest in Zhangjiakou because he had been running around for years, so Tang is not going elsewhere for the time being. As for his troops, including one brigade of Dong Futing, one brigade of Zheng Guilin, and Shao's regiment and Cui's regiment, totaling about eight thousand people, equipped with more than twenty cannons, most of them are stationed in Zhangbei. A portion, about a thousand people, were transferred to the outside of the Dajingmen in Zhangjiakou on the 15th and 16th of the month for unarmed training. When they handed in their guns, there was a conflict with the provincial army, which was quickly resolved. Zheng Guilin's unit was originally stationed in southern Tianjin. After a mutiny, they inquired their way to eastern Chahar and joined Tang. Now that Tang has handed over his troops to Chahar Province, Zheng fears for his own safety and has fled without a trace.

A Glimpse of the Current Situation in Zhangjiakou 84

Zhangjiakou is peaceful, and the market has returned to its state before the incident. There is no curfew at night. However, since the situation in eastern Chahar has become increasingly tense, the provincial government area has strengthened its defenses. The number of representatives staying in hotels and inns is not as high as it was during the Allied Army era. The weather is cold, and this year it is a little later than usual. According to visitors, heavy snow has fallen early in Zhangduogonghui, Jiabu Temple, and the area north of Zhangjiakou. The cold wind and snow are blowing every day, stinging the face and chilling the bones. Even wearing heavy fur coats is not enough to keep warm. Also, German-owned companies' cars travel between Zhangjiakou and Kulun to transport and sell goods, but due to the restrictions in Kulun, this has little positive impact on the Zhangjiakou market. (20th)

Tibetan Residents in Beiping Concerned About the Tibetan Situation 85

The Panchen Lama Will Return to Tibet via Nanjing from Bailing Temple

Li Erbukun Has Gone to Nanjing to Handle Tibetan Affairs

Beiping Correspondence: After the news of the Dalai Lama's death reached Beiping, the Beiping Office of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission immediately sent a telegram to the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission in Nanjing to inquire about the truth. As of today (21st), no reply telegram has arrived in Beiping. There are many lamas among the Tibetan residents in Beiping, who are very concerned about Tibetan affairs. Today (21st), Ms. Sun Bozhuang and others went to the Panchen Lama's office for discussions. According to reliable information from the Tibetan side, the Dalai Lama's representative, Gunqiao Zhongni, came to Beiping before the 20th and told people that the Dalai Lama was old and that the successor was very important in case of his death. The Dalai Lama did not favor the British during his life and originally wanted the central government to send troops to protect Tibet to avoid any incidents, but he was also concerned that his reach was too limited. Gunqiao Zhongni originally planned to go to Jiangxi to meet with Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to ask for instructions on everything, but unexpectedly the Dalai Lama passed away in Lhasa on the 17th. It is very difficult to produce a new Dalai Lama, because Lamaism forbids marriage, and the Dalai Lama has no wife or children, so there is no successor at the moment. The Silon Kagsha and Yicang are temporarily acting in charge of Tibetan political and religious affairs. However, it is not yet certain whether the Silon and others can manage everything during the transition period. Before the Dalai Lama died, he tried to persuade those with radical ideas among the Tibetan youth. Some Tibetan youths believed that the Dalai Lama was suppressing the youth, but there were no special actions. Now that the Dalai Lama is dead, according to religious customs, divination must be done to calculate where an infant is born. This infant is particularly divine and can point out what object and what name is. Then, everyone believes that the Dalai Lama has reincarnated, and the Silon Kagsha and Yicang go to welcome him back to Lhasa and perform the Hobilgan ceremony. Then, this infant is no longer a child of the people, but becomes the new Dalai Lama Living Buddha. After reaching adulthood, he can inherit the throne and take control of Tibetan political and religious power. However, it is not known when the new Dalai Lama will succeed to the throne. The British have been coveting Tibet for a long time. During the transition period, if the Silon and others can win the trust of the people and maintain order properly, then Tibet can still survive. Otherwise, the central government must send personnel to Tibet to assist the Silon and others in maintaining law and order, because the Tibetan issue is even more important than the issue of autonomy in Inner Mongolia. Currently, the Tibetan people are divided into two factions: one faction supports the Dalai Lama, mostly Red Sect followers, and most of them are from the former Tibet; the other faction supports the Panchen Lama, mostly Yellow Sect followers, and most of them are from the latter Tibet. In fact, neither faction has a clear system, and they do not care about politics, only knowing how to chant scriptures, but among the Tibetans, those who support the Dalai Lama are more numerous.

After the Dalai Lama's death, the center of gravity of Tibetan politics and religion was lost. Now that the Panchen Erdeni, who is staying in Bailing Temple, should be able to return to Tibet without any problems. This summer, the Panchen Lama sent someone to Tibet to negotiate, and three major temples expressed their welcome. Now that the Dalai Lama has passed away, someone is needed to preside over Tibetan politics, so it will be easier to realize it sooner. However, there are still some obstacles, which must be cleared in advance. The Panchen Lama will pass through Beiping two or three days after leaving the temple and then go to Nanjing to pay respects to the key figures of the National Government. In addition to reporting on the resolution of the Inner Mongolia autonomy issue, he will also ask for instructions on how to return to Tibet. According to A Shansheng, a Tibetan who is close to the Panchen Lama, the Panchen Lama has never interfered in Tibetan political and military affairs and only presided over religious affairs when he was in Tibet. This time when he returns to Tibet, he will take the will of the central government as his will, console the Tibetan people, and teach the new Dalai Lama the classics.

The Tibetan Office in Beiping has matters to discuss with Nanjing due to the Dalai Lama's death, and the Tibetan representative in Nanjing, Awang Zhaba, sent a telegram instructing Deputy Director Li Erbukun to go there. Li told reporters at the station today that after the Dalai Lama Living Buddha passed away, Tibetan political affairs were in charge of the Silon Kagsha. After the small Dalai Lama is born, the power will be handed back. He went to Nanjing this time at the invitation of Awang Zhaba, the Tibetan representative in Nanjing, to handle matters related to Tibet. (21st)

Guangdong Province's Winter Defense is Strict 86

Military Police Patrol Guangzhou City Day and Night

Personnel Sent to Build Defense Works in the Suburbs

The City of Nanxiong in Northern Guangdong Digs a Moat Around the City

Northeastern Trenches Can Accommodate Cars

Guangzhou Correspondence: According to a report, Guangdong Province authorities recently found slogans of the Fujian puppet organization in Jiangmen, and immediately ordered the military and police to take strict precautions. The Guangzhou Public Security Bureau also recently arrested the abbot of the Nengren Temple on Baiyun Mountain, Monk Manshu Jiedi, in the suburbs of Guangzhou. The monk, also known as Wan Quan, has been in the temple for several years. He does not seem like an outsider, has a little talent, and is boastful and impulsive. When Chen Mingshu was in charge of Guangdong's administration years ago, he had close contacts with him. This arrest is said to be related to the Fujian side. Another theory is that the monk has recently recruited many traveling monks, and the authorities fear that he has a political purpose, so they arrested him. After being arrested, he was detained in the Public Security Bureau and is being interrogated strictly. Since these cases occurred, the military and police have been even more strict in carrying out winter defense. Starting on the 16th, the Military Police Headquarters added five patrol teams to each team, with three people in each team, for a total of seventy-five teams, to patrol the city. In addition, five bicycle patrol teams were formed, with five bicycles in each team, patrolling from 10:00 AM every day and resting at 12:00 PM at night. The military police team has recently expanded to a total of fourteen teams, specializing in maintaining law and order in the city and dividing the area for defense. The first team is stationed in Meihua Village, the second team is stationed at the Guangzhou-Kowloon Station and Shenzhen Market, the third team is stationed at the Guangxi Guild Hall and Shiwitang, the fourth team is stationed at the Second Ordnance Factory in the eastern suburbs, the fifth team is stationed at the Pacification Office in the central district, the sixth team is stationed at Shougouling, the seventh team is stationed at the Yingde Mine, the eighth team is stationed at Yongshing Temple, the ninth team is stationed at the Zhaoqing Guild Hall, the tenth team is stationed at the Bayi Guild Hall, the eleventh team is stationed at the Provincial Government and the Southwestern Executive Department of the Party, the twelfth team is stationed at Yantang, the thirteenth team is stationed at the Radio Station in the northern suburbs, and the fourteenth team is stationed at the Headquarters of the First Army Group. As for Yaotou, Geshan, Xiaogang, Shayuan, Erchongkou and other places in the suburbs of Henan, the Public Security Bureau sent two squads of security teams to guard the key points and added detectives to patrol secretly. Panyu County's third and sixth districts, including Huatai, Fangcun, and other twenty-four villages, were also instructed to organize a joint defense to prevent bandits from mixing in. Iron wire nets have recently been added to the waterways of the provincial river by personnel from the Fleet Command and the teaching division of engineers. The defenses are also said to be tight.

Guangdong Province's border defense work has been booming in recent days. It is said that Nanxiong, in the north of the Beijiang River, which is adjacent to southern Jiangxi, began digging trenches at the beginning of this month. The Independent Third Division of the Defense Army, together with various mass organizations, is actively digging trenches and collecting conscripted labor. A total of 20,000 young men were conscripted, and funds were raised from all walks of life. The moat outside the city is being constructed in nine sections. The depth of the moat is over nine feet, the width is seventeen or eight feet, and the length is a circle around the city. In addition, there are many defense works set up in the Dongjiang area, and three lines of defense are arranged. In Fengshun alone, in addition to dangerous trenches, there are more than a hundred gun emplacements. Cars can be used to transport goods inside the trenches. The authorities have purchased a large number of transport vehicles in recent days and handed them over to the transport station for distribution to the front lines. The first batch of sixteen six-wheeled heavy trucks has been transported, and the second batch of twenty has also been. In addition, cannonballs and military supplies are being transported to Shantou by the An An warship for transfer to the front lines for use. As for Humen, which is the gateway to Guangdong by sea, a general curfew has been imposed at night recently. If any suspicious ships pass by, they are ordered to stop and wait for inspection to prevent bandits from transporting them secretly. (December 20th)

Wang Afu and Hua Jusheng, two hooligans, previously forged theater tickets for the Huiming Theater outside the West Gate. The related persons Yu Fuquan and Tie Changwang were sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment with two years of probation. After the verdict, Wang Afu was ordered to be sent back to prison.

Young Maid Abused to Death 92

Zhu Changhou of No. 33, Chengquan Lane, Wuyi, is engaged in business in Hankou. His wife, Zhu Wang, nicknamed Wang Erjie, has two sons and one daughter who live in Changzhou. Because he was coveted by bandits, he suddenly received a letter from bandits a few days ago, with many threatening words, demanding 500 yuan. Luogen was extremely panicked, but had no choice but to put it aside and ignore it. Three days later, he received another letter, with even more violent language. Wu was afraid of accidents and went to report to the District Office, requesting an investigation. On the 20th, Wu suddenly received a third letter, which stated that there was no news from the previous two letters. This is the final warning, and he was asked to bring the money to the Ximen Xie Shui Lujiiao within three days to discuss the matter. Otherwise, there will be disadvantages. At this point, Wu gained some insight. He remembered that the monk Zongde of the nearby Guanyin Temple was not pure in his six senses and acted irregularly, and suspected that he was the one who did it. He reported his suspicions to the District Office and forwarded it to the jurisdictional Public Security Bureau. The Public Security Bureau immediately sent police to arrest the suspect monk and take him to the District Office. After detailed questioning and verification of the handwriting, it seemed similar. Just as they were about to send him to the Public Security Bureau, the monk suddenly took advantage of people's lack of preparation and escaped. By the time they noticed, there was no trace of him. Now, Xu Jingyu, the district chief of the district, has presented a request to the county for punishment, and has reported to the authorities requesting a search.

Re-inspection of Foreign Ships Going to Fujian 104

Inspected in the Sandu Sea Area

When the British merchant ship Yihe Hengsheng arrived in Fuzhou, it was inspected by the Navy's Yixian ship. The British Consul in Nanjing protested and the inspection was stopped. Afterwards, when the Jiesheng ship entered and exited, the inspection was stopped. Recently, due to the outbreak of war rituals in Fujian, the central government, in order to strictly prevent smuggling on the sea, re-negotiated with the British Consulate to implement inspections on foreign ships traveling between Shanghai and Fujian. The situation is recorded separately as follows:

Customs Inspection of Outbound Goods 105

Recently, among goods shipped from Shanghai to Fuzhou, aside from textiles, food is the most prevalent. White rice and flour are shipped in the largest quantities. Traditionally, food exports haven't required customs inspection. However, due to a central government order and deep concerns about the possibility of smuggling military supplies along with rice and flour destined for Fujian Province, customs inspection is now required. Food export inspection has been implemented, and this is the first time. Therefore, for several days, any goods being shipped to Fujian are subject to inspection by customs officers, and the enforcement is quite strict.

Inspection of Merchant Ships 106

Currently, only Jardine Matheson's "Chefoo" vessel operates between Shanghai and Fuzhou. Recently, due to the serious situation, consultations with various shipping companies have resulted in an agreement that both inbound and outbound ships must be inspected at Sandu Ao. Navy personnel will board the ships to conduct thorough searches, especially of passengers and their luggage. However, cargo holds are exempt from inspection. During its recent trip to Shanghai, Jardine Matheson's "Chefoo" was inspected again when passing through Sandu Ao.

Weak Military Strength in Fujian 108

Outward Expansion Unlikely

According to the "New Voice Society," a semi-official source reported yesterday morning that the deployments of the 19th Route Army and the Communist bandits in northern Fujian indicate that the 19th Route Army has not yet formally engaged the Central Army. Therefore, rumors of engagement with the Central Army and a three-pronged northern offensive are untrue. The current deployments of the 19th Route Army and Communist bandits are as follows: (A) The 19th Route Army has a total strength of 45,000 men, including 15,000 men reorganized from the old units of Zhang Zhen and Chen Guohui. Their recent deployments are: one brigade of Zhang's old units stationed in Yunxiao and Zhao'an in southern Fujian; one division of Gao Yi and Chen Guohui's old units stationed in Xiamen, Dehua, Yongchun, Anxi, and Tong'an; one division of the 19th Route Army stationed in Yanping, Jianning, and Shaowu in northwestern Fujian; one division and one brigade of the 19th Route Army stationed in Fuzhou and Putian; and one division and one brigade of the 19th Route Army stationed in Zhangzhou, Changtai, Huacun, Zhangping, Ningyang, Hexi, and Shizhong in southern Fujian. As for the Communist bandits, remnants have some influence in Zhenghe in northern Fujian and Qingyuan and Longquan near the Zhejiang border. The bandit forces in the Jiangxi area, below Jianchang, along the coast, and along the Yangtze River in western Fujian, are relatively strong. They are currently attempting to advance northward from Jianchang and disturb the Zhejiang border. Therefore, recent rumors of contact between Fujian and Zhejiang actually refer to the Communist bandits' advance into Zhejiang and clashes with the Central Army. It is also reported that the Fujian army, except for the advance in the Yanping and Jian'ou areas and slight contact with Liu Heding's troops within Fujian, has not encountered the Central Army.

Ministry Personnel Arrive in Shanghai to Investigate Labor Dispute at Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Factory in Songhu 110

Yesterday, Further Efforts to Persuade Workers to Return to Work Failed

Negotiations to Resolve the Issue Scheduled for Today

According to "Dagong News," workers at the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway factory in Zhanghuabang, Wusong, declared a strike on the 18th of this month in protest against the transfer of staff by Chief of General Affairs Mo Heng and the suppression of the labor movement. They demanded Mo Heng's dismissal. Yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, representatives from the railway administration, the Party branch, and the labor union went to Wusong to persuade the workers to return to work, but to no avail. The Ministry of Railways has dispatched counselors Wang Wenbin and Zhang Weici to conduct a thorough investigation. The details are reported below.

Further Efforts to Persuade Workers to Return to Work Failed 111

Since the labor dispute broke out at the Wusong factory, the railway administration has consulted with the special Party branches and labor unions of the two railways to find a solution. A decision was made to form an investigation committee to thoroughly investigate the workers' accusations against Mo Heng. The workers were urged to return to work first, and then the investigation would proceed. Yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, Yuan Boyang, Wang Bi, Fan Shouzheng, and Lu Baogan from the railway administration, along with Zou Kexin, Chen Chengshi, and Li Dasan from the Party branches of the two railways, and Liang Luoheng and Chen Bohua from the labor unions of the two railways, traveled to the Zhanghuabang factory. Representatives from the railway administration summoned the foremen of each workshop, while representatives from the Party branch and the labor union summoned all staff of the Wusong office of the railway union, to persuade them to return to work separately. However, the workers insisted that Mo Heng must be dismissed first before they would agree to return to work, so the efforts were unsuccessful. All workers continued their strike.

Special Envoys from the Ministry of Railways Arrive in Shanghai 112

Railway Minister Gu Mengyu, after receiving reports from the directors of the two railways, Huang Bobiao, and the special Party branches and labor unions of the two railways, regarding the strike at the Wusong factory in protest against the removal of Mo Heng, the Chief of General Affairs and Chief of the Materials Department, immediately telegraphed the railway administration to properly restrain the situation and dispatched counselors Wang Wenbin and Zhang Weici to Shanghai for a thorough investigation. They arrived in Shanghai at 1:00 PM yesterday. They first went to the railway administration to inquire about the details and then proceeded to the Zhanghuabang factory to investigate the truth of the labor dispute in order to find a solution.

Negotiations Scheduled for Today 113

After arriving in Shanghai, the Ministry of Railways' counselors Wang Wenbin and Zhang Weici, in addition to investigating the circumstances of the labor dispute from all parties in order to find a solution, scheduled a meeting for today with representatives from the railway administration, the Party branch, the labor union, and the workers to discuss a resolution. At the same time, they will thoroughly investigate the workers' accusations against Mo Heng in order to clarify the truth.

Railway Administration Statement of Facts 114

A reporter from "Dagong News" visited the railway administration yesterday. According to a person in charge, the recent news reports about the labor dispute at the two railways' factory did not reflect the facts. The workers at the Wusong factory and the Materials Department suddenly went on strike to protest the transfer of staff member Cao Wenkui by Chief of General Affairs Mo Heng. The railway administration has the inherent administrative power to transfer staff. If they are dissatisfied with the railway administration's actions, they should make a formal complaint. The workers' sudden strike is unfortunate because they did not follow proper procedures. The claim that Mo Heng purchased inferior materials that could not be used since he also became Chief of the Materials Department is a deliberate slander. The Ministry of Railways has sent personnel to Shanghai to investigate, and the truth will be revealed. However, it would be incorrect to dismiss Mo Heng before the investigation is complete.

Silk Market Plunges, Factories Close, Unions Jointly Petition the Party and Government 117

Unemployment Increases by 60,000, Causing Panic About Livelihood

Request to Forward Petition to Central Government for Assistance

According to "Dagong News," Shanghai's silk reeling factories have been affected by the Japanese silk market and exports to Europe and America, leading to a sharp drop in silk prices. As a result, factories are closing one after another, and unemployment has increased by 60,000, causing panic about livelihoods. Yesterday morning, silk reeling unions jointly petitioned Party and government organs, requesting that the central government be informed and assistance be provided. The details are as follows:

Joint Petition Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Chen Xiupu, Le Xiaorong, Chen Yundi, Yuan Yunlong, Yang Gengti, and Wu Suzhen, the directors of the silk reeling unions of the third, fourth, and sixth districts of Shanghai, led more than 31 representatives from various factories to petition the municipal Party headquarters. They requested that the central government be promptly notified and assistance be provided to the silk industry, and that the factories be ordered to reopen to maintain the livelihoods of the workers. Zhu Yangwu, a cadre of the Civil Affairs Section, received them and promised to submit the petition to the Executive Committee for consideration. The representatives expressed their satisfaction and then went to the municipal government to petition. Representatives from the Second Section received them and promised to submit the difficulties of the silk industry to the mayor for review and action. The representatives also went to the Social Affairs Bureau to make the same petition.

Request for Relief Yesterday, the Industrial Union of the silk reeling industry of the fourth and sixth districts of Shanghai submitted a document to the municipal Party headquarters, the municipal government, and the Social Affairs Bureau, stating: "Regarding the request for relief for unemployment and the maintenance of workers' livelihoods, the more than 60,000 male members of our union depend on silk factories for a living. In recent years, due to the slump in the silk market, the factories have repeatedly failed. Fortunately, the government has provided assistance twice, allowing them to barely maintain work for more than half of the workers. Tens of thousands of workers rely on this to eke out a living. Since the autumn of this year, silk prices have plummeted, setting a new low. The factories intended to continue to operate, but bankruptcies have followed one another, and closures and shutdowns have occurred one after another. In each district, fewer than ten factories are barely maintaining operations. The situation is precarious and cannot be described in words. If this continues, all factories in the city will shut down completely in the near future. Tens of thousands of workers in our union will all be unemployed, their livelihoods will be without support, and they will all starve to death. All the workers are worried and anxious, and they come to the union to ask for assistance. We are horrified by this situation. If we do not seek relief urgently, it is inevitable that they will take risks, which will affect social stability. Therefore, after a joint meeting, we unanimously decided to request that your departments (government bureaus) telegraph the central government to provide relief to maintain the livelihoods of the workers and ensure social order. We are eagerly awaiting orders."

Cotton Control Committee's Efforts to Stabilize Yarn Prices 118

Remarks by Committee Member Li Shengbo

According to "Dagong News," due to the excessive amount of yarn stored in the Hua Shang Yarn and Cloth Exchange, which affected the market, the Cotton Control Committee established the He Xing Company to purchase some of the stored yarn to facilitate circulation. The committee also requested the Ministry of Industry to order the exchange to stop accepting new yarn from October onwards to show restriction. A reporter from "Dagong News" visited the Cotton Control Committee yesterday to inquire about the details of this matter and future solutions. Committee member Li Shengbo received him and provided a detailed explanation.

Reasons for Purchasing Stored Yarn 119

Li said that when yarn prices were extremely depressed, it was the beginning of the autumn sales season. However, because market prices were falling daily, yarn merchants were reluctant to operate, and farmers had no yarn to weave. As a result, the yarn stored in the Yarn and Cloth Exchange became increasingly large. At that time, the exchange had 36,000 bales of yarn in storage, and the market was falling more and more sharply. In order to stabilize the market, the Cotton Control Committee decided to negotiate with the Yong'an in Shanghai, the Qingfeng in Wuxi, and the Dasheng in Nantong to organize the He Xing Company. The He Xing company bought 15,000 bales of yarn to stabilize market prices, allowing the yarn merchants to boldly purchase the remaining 21,000 bales of yarn.

Continued Delivery of New Yarn in Violation of the Agreement 120

Unexpectedly, after He Xing Company purchased 15,000 bales, Shen Xin Factory continued to deliver 8,000 bales of substandard yarn. The Yarn and Cloth Exchange did not stop it, limited by regulations. In view of this situation, the Cotton Control Committee requested the Ministry of Industry to order the exchange not to accept new yarn for new transactions from October onwards. In addition, the Yarn Manufacturers Association and other associations would work together to clear the newly delivered 8,000 bales of yarn to a total of 29,000 bales, because the Yarn Manufacturers Association passed a resolution in July to restrict factories from delivering new yarn.

Methods for Clearing Stored Yarn 121

After discussions among the Cotton Control Committee, the Yarn Manufacturers Association, and the Yarn and Cloth Exchange, it was decided that the Shen Xin Factory would take 7,000 bales of the yarn, and the exchange would take 10,000 bales. The price was set at 170 yuan per bale. This price is the lowest in 15 years. Even if it were sold in the interior, there would be no loss. The contract has been signed and submitted to the Ministry of Industry for record. It is planned to clear it by the end of this year.

Losses from Purchasing Stored Yarn 122

Of the 15,000 bales of yarn purchased, 12,000 bales have been sold in various regions. The remaining 3,000 bales have not been sold, but it has been decided to clear it by the end of this year. On each bale, there will be a loss of six or seven yuan for a total of over 100,000 yuan. At the beginning of the Cotton Control Committee's actions, the committee planned to request a 4 million yuan appropriation from the central government to prepare for the purchase of this inferior yarn. However, due to the change in finance ministers from Song Ziwen to Kong Xiangxi, and the Fujian Incident, the government's finances were exhausted, so the plan was put on hold. Otherwise, this difficulty would have been resolved earlier.

Standard Grading Restrictions 123

In order to prevent such problems in the future, the Cotton Control Committee plans to revise the current standards of the exchange using scientific methods. Requirements such as tensile strength, fiber color, and brand will be combined. The new standards and regulations are being drafted. After being approved by the exchange, they will be submitted to the Ministry of Industry for record and implementation. Generally, one yuan is one level. If the cotton is less than 70 percent, it does not meet the standards, and the exchange will not accept it. The Cotton Control Committee plans to send eight experts to jointly appraise the cotton at the exchange.

Shanghai Telephone Company Notice to Pudong Users 124

Definite Date for Disconnecting and Reconnecting Phones

Separate Letter to Follow

The Shanghai Telephone Company issued a notice to Pudong users stating, "We provide services to organizations within the Public and French Concessions. However, for the convenience of users with houses in Pudong, we have also provided telephone services in Pudong for many years. Since April 19, 1933, when we signed a temporary agreement with the Chinese authorities, one of the clauses stated that the Ministry of Communications' Telephone Bureau could request the removal of all Pudong telephones with 30 days' notice. We issued a special notice to all affected users regarding this matter on April 19, 1933. We have now received a notice from the Ministry of Communications' Shanghai Telephone Bureau stating that the Bureau plans to take over our Pudong telephones in early 1934. After the takeover, all Pudong telephones will become part of the Ministry of Communications' Telephone Bureau's mutual communication system with our company. Therefore, the Shanghai Telephone Company is issuing this notice to all users affected by the above actions of the Ministry of Communications' Telephone Bureau. Your contract with our company will also be terminated when this change takes place. Afterwards, if you still require telephone service, please contact the Ministry of Communications' Shanghai Telephone Bureau. We are currently discussing with the Ministry of Communications' Shanghai Telephone Bureau the disconnection from our system and reconnection to the Ministry of Communications' Telephone Bureau's system for all users who will continue to receive service from that Bureau. The disconnection and reconnection will be done at night on the agreed date. We will send you another letter to inform you of the exact date of termination of the contract. Please accept our best wishes." Pan Lai, Director of the Business Department.

Indian, Sun Tai Xin, Convicted of Anti-British Activities 125

Trial Held at the British Police Court Yesterday

According to the "Great American Evening Post," the Indian, Sun Tai Xin, was arrested after distributing anti-British leaflets in Shanghai. He had been sought by the Public Concession Police for two years. The British Consulate Police Court held a trial this morning (the 22nd). Sun Tai Xin distributed seditious printed materials at the corner of Sichuan Road and Qiujiang Road in 1930. He was found guilty, so the court transferred him to the British Assize Court for trial. The date will be determined later. Today, Sun Tai Xin stood in the dock and listened to the testimony of the witnesses. When the royal lawyer asked him questions, he always answered, "No problem." When asked about his crimes, Sun Tai Xin raised his head and replied, "There is nothing in the leaflets that is hostile to the British government. It is the same as the current movement in India. The British government's actions in India and the bloodshed in India are all written in it." The court then warned him that the purpose of the trial was to determine whether he had committed the crimes he was accused of. Sun Tai Xin then said, "I was accused of distributing leaflets, so I must explain the reasons for distributing leaflets. The appeals of the Indian people cannot be heard, so I distributed leaflets to tell the world. There is nothing else to say." The defendant was arrested near Bazhi Road for fighting and committing assault, so the Police Court will also hold a hearing on the illegal assault case next Thursday.

Yao Wennan and Others Request That the Municipal Government Issue Land Certificates Locally 131

Recounting the Difficulties Faced by Villagers in Going to Government Offices

Due to the Relocation of the Land Bureau to the City Center

Yao Wennan, the former Chief Director of the Land Survey Bureau, along with directors Qin Xitian, Hu Renfeng, Shen Zhou, Pan Liangshi, Li Hongzhu, Zhang Zongfu, Liu Donghai, and others, submitted a petition to the municipal government requesting that land ownership certificates be issued locally because the Land Bureau has moved to the city center, making it difficult for villagers to obtain their certificates. The original text is as follows: "It is heard that your government has moved to the city center, and all bureaus should follow. The plan for Greater Shanghai is admired by scholars and people. However, it is known that land occupation certificates in various rural areas are gradually completed, and the villagers must all go to the bureau to receive the certificates. The city center area is still remote. For those who are far from the rural areas, it is nearly a hundred miles away. Even for those who are nearby, it is thirty or forty miles away. There are rental boundaries in the middle, the roads are many, and the vehicles are mixed. The villagers who go to the bureau to receive certificates must be guided. They have to run around for a day to arrive. They can not return to the village on the same day, and the cost of food and accommodation is not less than three or four yuan. If the procedures are wrong, it will cost them several days and much more money. At this time of economic panic in the countryside, how can we allow this unexpected loss? According to the political system, it does not seem appropriate. For example, the households in the Caojing area who have not yet received certificates cannot get to the bureau on foot in less than three or four hours. When they get to the bureau gate, the policemen stand there, and they are afraid to look at them. The villagers are illiterate, and they run around blindly. Fortunately, a paper is thrown in, and they spend two or three hours starving and waiting for orders. It can be said that the time of one day's work has been completely consumed. If the grain certificate is incomplete, the contract does not match, or the single land does not match, they will go back and forth four or five times, spending dozens of yuan. By the time a certificate is in hand, the field price has lost seventy or eighty percent of its value. The villagers resent the directors and criticize them for being the culprits of evil. At the beginning of the directors' establishment of the land survey, their goal was to benefit the people, but today it has become a government that harms the people. Good causes lead to evil consequences, which is what the directors are heartbroken day and night. Moreover, the distance from Yangsi and other districts to the city center is several times farther than the distance from Caojing to the South Shanghai District. The people are limited in their strength. How can they bear this? Therefore, we dare to ask the mayor to order the director of the Land Bureau to appoint an appropriate official to meet with the municipal committee members of each district to issue the certificates locally, and properly handle any disputes, to save the villagers' financial resources and to relieve the directors' guilt. The villagers are fortunate, and the directors are also fortunate. After the Land Bureau moves north, please set up an office in the South Shanghai District so that the command can be prompt in the event of measurement and remeasurement. Officials and people will not be isolated, the cost is saved, and the effect is significant, not just to benefit the villagers. These are our humble opinions. We sincerely hope that you will adopt and implement them. We are very grateful."
