Amendment of Stamp Tax Regulations 134

Joint Promulgation by the Ministries of Finance and Law

The Ministries of Finance and Justice, considering that the current Provisional Stamp Tax Regulations have encountered many obstacles in their enforcement due to Article 4 of the Implementation Rules and Penalty Regulations, which stipulates that judicial organs' rulings regarding stamp tax penalties cannot be appealed, have jointly deliberated and amended the said rules. They have submitted the amendment to the Executive Yuan for forwarding to the National Government for record. The amended text is excerpted below: (Article 1) When judicial authorities discover or receive reports during the trial of lawsuits regarding matters of failure to affix stamps in accordance with the Provisional Stamp Tax Regulations, they shall impose fines in accordance with the said regulations. (Article 2) Penalties imposed by judicial authorities under the Provisional Stamp Tax Regulations shall be executed by rulings. (Article 3) When judicial authorities encounter violations of the Provisional Stamp Tax Regulations by litigants, they shall impose penalties in accordance with the said regulations without delaying the progress of the lawsuit. (Article 4) Appeals against the rulings in Article 2 may be lodged with the competent higher court within five days. No further appeals shall be permitted against the court's ruling. (Article 5) Judicial authorities may stipulate a deadline for the payment of fines imposed under the Provisional Stamp Tax Regulations. Failure to pay within the deadline shall result in compulsory execution. (Article 6) Fines imposed under the Provisional Stamp Tax Regulations, except for those reported by informers, who shall receive 40% as a reward, shall have 40% allocated to the judicial organ's operating expenses. The remainder shall be used to purchase judicial stamps and included under judicial revenue, with monthly reports made on the percentages of the aforementioned fines, based on the actual amount received. (Article 7) These rules shall come into effect from the date of promulgation.

National Chamber of Commerce Federation Appeals to the Executive Yuan and Ministries to Return Fines Levied on Native Sugar from Qinzhou and Lianzhou 135

The Qinzhou and Lianzhou chambers of commerce in Guangdong province have jointly dispatched representatives, led by Pang Songhui, to petition in Beijing regarding the case of native sugar from Qinzhou and Lianzhou being transported to Shanghai, where the Jianghai Customs deemed it adulterated with foreign sugar and levied fines. Mr. Pang has already arrived in Shanghai and has sought assistance from the National Chamber of Commerce Federation and the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. The National Chamber of Commerce Federation, considering the matter to be of concern to the national sugar industry, has telegraphed the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Customs Administration, requesting them to uphold justice and redress the grievances. The original telegram is recorded below: To the esteemed Executive Yuan, Ministry of Finance, Ministry of Industry, and Customs Administration in Nanjing: We have recently received a joint letter from the Beihai Municipal Chamber of Commerce in Guangdong and the Hepu County Chamber of Commerce, stating that the Qinzhou and Lianzhou sugar merchant Guangyitang reported receiving letters from their counterparts Heli, Henghelong, Guangchanghe, and Heyi, stating that between July and September of this year, they transported native white sugar from Beihai to Shanghai a total of five times. Each time, they reported the goods to the Beihai Customs for inspection, confirming that it was pure native sugar and paying the transit tax in accordance with regulations before being allowed to proceed. Unexpectedly, upon direct arrival at Shanghai, the Jianghai Customs Tax Office completely detained the goods, claiming they contained 10% to 20% foreign sugar, and levied fines totaling 1,560 yuan and a supplementary tax of 1,957 yuan. The method used to distinguish between native and foreign sugar was without standards and prone to errors. The merchants have jointly submitted appeals and telegrams, but the matter has not been resolved after more than a month. The merchants are innocent and have suffered significant losses, forcing them to temporarily suspend business pending relief. Therefore, they have specially provided a list of fines levied on each merchant and requested verification. They implore you to forward the letter to the Beihai Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the various Qinzhou and Lianzhou chambers of commerce, and request them to submit it to the Ministry of Finance and the Customs Administration, ordering the Jianghai Customs Tax Office to return the fines in full to demonstrate fairness. It is noted that Beihai is an important port for the export of Chinese native sugar, and the Beihai Customs is located close to the sugar-producing area. They have a clear understanding of the composition of native sugar and the differences between it and foreign sugar. Therefore, previous declarations of native sugar have always been inspected and released without error or difficulty. Now that the goods have been directly transported to Shanghai, the Jianghai Customs Tax Office claims they contain foreign sugar and levies substantial fines, clearly abusing their authority and undermining domestic products. If this is not stopped according to the law, how can farmers and merchants have peace of mind? Therefore, we have specially recorded the letter and forwarded it to you to alleviate the merchants' difficulties. Upon approval, the association investigated and found that since the Jianghai Customs levied fines on native sugar, sugar merchants have suspended transport, incurring significant losses. Furthermore, the farmers and laborers in more than ten counties who rely on the sugar industry for their livelihoods are at risk of unemployment and bankruptcy. Their livelihoods and social order are all seriously affected. Based on the letter, we believe that the matter concerns the livelihoods of farmers and merchants in more than ten counties. Therefore, we have jointly convened the Hepu County Chamber of Commerce, sugar industry guilds, and all sugar merchants to discuss relief measures. A total of four resolutions were reached: (1) Request the Ministry of Finance to correct the erroneous methods used by the Jianghai Customs to distinguish between native and foreign sugar. (2) Request the Ministry of Finance to order the Jianghai Customs to release the native sugar of Beihai sugar merchants and return all past fines and supplementary taxes. (3) Request the Executive Yuan to instruct all customs offices nationwide to ensure the safety of native sugar exports and imports and not to deliberately create difficulties. (4) Request the Central Government to issue a clear order exempting native sugar from export and transit taxes and to establish export incentive measures for native sugar. These resolutions were unanimously passed and, in addition to telegrams and separate submissions, we have specially recorded the case and forwarded it to your association, and dispatched representative Pang Songhui to personally present the case. We implore you to provide effective assistance so that this case can be thoroughly resolved as soon as possible, which would not only benefit the Qinzhou and Lianzhou sugar industries but also the national industry. The representative Pang Songhui has also arrived at the association and provided further details, which have been approved. This case was previously received from the Haikou Municipal Chamber of Commerce in Guangdong, requesting forwarding to the association. The association has repeatedly telegraphed the case to the department without a response. Based on the letter, we hereby re-telegraphically submit it to your esteemed Executive Yuan for review and approval. We implore you to quickly order the Qionghai Customs to release the detained native sugar, return the collected fines, and exempt native sugar from export and transit taxes, in order to encourage domestic products and maintain the people's livelihood. This is our earnest prayer. [Signed] Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce Federation of the Republic of China [Seal]

Over fifty villagers, including Yin Fugen from Yuansha Lujiage in Jiangwan District, have petitioned the Jiangwan District Municipal Committee to forward their request to the Municipal Bureau of Public Works to cease the unauthorized demolition of dikes and private occupation of farmland by the contractor during the dredging of the river, which is harming farmland. The original text reads: "We, the villagers, have lived along the Qiongjiang River in Jiangwan for generations, earning our livelihoods through farming. All our farmland lies north and south of the Qiongjiang River. The Qiongjiang River connects to the Huangpu River in the south, and the tide ebbs and flows easily. Therefore, high dikes have been built on both banks to prevent flooding. During the two typhoons this autumn, the tide rose high, but our farmland was not flooded, thanks to the protection of the high dikes. Now, the contractor, under the pretext of dredging the Qiongjiang River, is arbitrarily demolishing the dikes and privately transporting the mud, not only damaging our property but also depriving the farmland on both sides of its protection, which is at risk of flooding at any time. The notice from the Municipal Bureau of Public Works states: 'It is noted that the land in the central district of the city is low-lying and in urgent need of soil to raise it for construction. The Yuansha Creek and the Qiongjiang River west of Songhu Road are suitable for dredging and extracting soil. The Bureau has contracted out the project, which will commence soon. Once this river is dredged, it will greatly facilitate transportation and irrigation, which is a win-win situation. The high soil on both sides of the Yuanchang River also needs to be leveled for cultivation. If there are losses to crops, it concerns major construction projects. All residents of both townships must not obstruct the project, lest there be inconvenience. This is hereby announced.' Therefore, the notice from the Bureau of Public Works only mentions dredging and soil extraction and does not mention demolishing the dikes. However, before the contractor has started the dredging project, they have set up tracks and seized the soil on both banks, intending to transport and sell it privately, which is clearly an act of encroaching on private property and harming farmland. Therefore, we appeal to the Municipal Committee to forward this request to the Municipal Bureau of Public Works, ordering them to cease the demolition of the dikes and severely punish the foreman, in order to protect private property. This would be a virtuous act." It is reported that the District Municipal Committee has forwarded the above-mentioned dispute to the Municipal Bureau of Public Works for investigation and resolution.

Sudden Tragic Death of He Shiliang, Chief Comprador of Jardine Matheson in Hong Kong 140

Telegram Did Not Mention Details, Shanghai Office in Shock

He Shiliang, the chief comprador of Jardine Matheson in Hong Kong, had been in service for decades and was a leading figure among the Chinese merchants in Hong Kong. Yesterday, a sudden telegram from Hong Kong reported He Shiliang's tragic death. The circumstances were bizarre, and the Shanghai office was shocked upon receiving the news. Details are recorded below:

Nephew of He Dong 141

Jardine Matheson & Co., a British firm, has its largest shipping and import-export business in Hong Kong, followed by Shanghai. The Chinese name of Jardine Matheson in Hong Kong is Zha Dian. Its large business and strong influence rank first among British firms. The chief comprador, He Shiliang, is the nephew of Sir He Dong, a wealthy gentleman in Hong Kong. When Jardine Matheson first started its shipping business in China, He Shiliang's grandfather was a partner in the business. He served as the Chinese manager, both as a shareholder and comprador. His descendants have inherited this position to this day. He Shiliang is the nephew of Sir He Dong and comes from a very wealthy family. He also holds a significant position in the Hong Kong commercial community.

Great Enterprise 142

Jardine Matheson's granulated sugar is still widely sold in the Yangtze River basin and is very popular. He Shiliang's grandfather founded its sugar factory, which was later merged into Jardine Matheson. He Shiliang's father, He Fu, had a prominent reputation in Hong Kong. He Shiliang succeeded his father's position and expanded the business even further. He was involved in even more commercial activities. He had a relationship with most of the major commercial ventures in Hong Kong. As the chief comprador of Jardine Matheson, he handled his duties very well. Many of the staff working in the company are the children and relatives of the elite who had studied abroad. His brother, He Yuezhou, is in charge of the shipping business. He Shiliang is involved in many other businesses, but he mainly oversees them.

Shocking News 143

He Shiliang was over forty years old and a very handsome man. The Westerners at Jardine Matheson's head office relied on him and regarded him as an important leader in their Chinese operations. All the Chinese staff working on land and sea in the company obeyed and supported He Shiliang because he was always fair and impartial. Yesterday, the Shanghai office suddenly received an urgent telegram in English from Hong Kong. The translation only had a few words: "Hong Kong manager He Shiliang tragically died." No other details were provided. The senior management and compradores in the Shanghai office were saddened and filled with suspicion upon receiving the news.

Telegraphic Inquiry 144

Yesterday, the senior management of Jardine Matheson in Shanghai telegraphed the Hong Kong office to inquire about the circumstances of He Shiliang's tragic death. It is still unclear whether his death was due to suicide or homicide. The truth will not be known until the reply telegram arrives in Shanghai. The company's Hong Kong liner will arrive in Shanghai on Sunday, and more information about this matter will be available then.

Various Rumors 145

The reporter inquired about the cause of He Shiliang's death from various sources, but no one could confirm the truth of his tragic death. However, according to those who knew He Shiliang well, he had many private businesses in Hong Kong. This year, all industries have been in decline, and all of his businesses have been affected by the situation, suffering significant losses. As the end of the year approaches, He Shiliang's total losses have reached several million dollars, and he was unable to cover them. Therefore, he resorted to tragic death. However, it is difficult to say for sure whether this is the case. The truth will be known in a day or two. He Shiliang's death has also had a significant impact on the Hong Kong market.

Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department, along with Wang Yingbin, Secretary of the Construction Department, and Du Zhenyuan, Director of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway Bureau, came to Shanghai and hosted a reception for the local press at the Bank Club on Hong Kong Road yesterday afternoon. They reported on the construction of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway and invited the press to participate in the opening ceremony and tour the scenic spots along the railway.

Guest List 148

The following guests attended: Ma Yinliang, Zhang Shutong, Zhao Junhao, Sun Daosheng, Jin Huating, Gu Angruo, Sun Enlin, Wang Boqi, Wang Zhongwei, Li Boyu, Wang Weizhen, Chen Dazai, Zhang Zhuping, Xiong Shaohao, Pan Gongbi, Xiang Yuancun, Chu Baoheng, Jiang Xiangqing, Liu Tong, Zheng Xitao, Wu Baoji, Dong Xian'guang, Pan Gongzhan, He Xiya, Xu Zhuodai, Guan Jian, Qian Cangshuo, Hu Hanzhu, Jiang Zongdao, Zeng Xubai, Chen Yaozhu, Wang Tiran, Cui Wanqiu, and Wang Zilian, Zheng Yaonan, Lu Meiseng, Yao Junwei and others, more than forty people from advertising industry.

Speeches by Hosts and Guests 149

During the reception, Director Zeng delivered a welcoming speech, stating that the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway is 370 kilometers long, with rails weighing 35 pounds per yard and cars weighing 15 and 20 tons. It cost over 12 million yuan. Although the scale is small, the capital and design are all from Chinese sources, which is something to be proud of. The business prospects are also quite promising. Although there may not be immediate profits, it is safe to say that there will be no losses. The cost-effectiveness of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway has changed people's perception of railways. In the past, it was believed that it was difficult to make profits from railways, but now many others are following suit, such as the Wuhu-Zhejiang, Yuping, and Longyan-Zhangzhou railways, as well as the continued completion of the Hangzhou-Ningbo and Guangdong-Hankou railways. The colleagues are unsure whether the management of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway is appropriate and hope that the gentlemen can conduct on-site inspections and provide guidance so that we may follow. Furthermore, Zhejiang Province has magnificent scenery that is worth visiting. The gentlemen should take time out of their busy schedules to express their feelings. After the Fujian Incident, there have been rumors of tensions on the Zhejiang border. In reality, Zhejiang Province has a strict defense system and there is absolutely no cause for concern. The gentlemen will experience the reality of Zhejiang's tranquility and stability. Then, Zhang Zhuping gave a speech on behalf of the press to express his gratitude.

Xu Ji Lawsuit Opens 152

Court Prohibits Public Attendance

Trial Postponed to Next Year

Mrs. Xu Li, accompanied by her daughter Xu Yuying, hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Ji Juemi for offenses against public morals. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, Judge Xiao Xiexun of the First Special District District Court held the trial in the Eighth Tribunal. The plaintiffs, mother and daughter, along with their lawyer Cao Yongsheng, and the defendants Ji Juemi and the second defendant, Mrs. Yu Xiaomei, and their lawyers Xue Dubi and Shan Yuhua, all arrived at the court with their respective representatives. The audience also flocked to the courtroom, causing it to be overcrowded. To maintain order, the authorities temporarily dispatched additional law enforcement officers, led by a police officer from the Western District, to the courtroom. They also stationed guards at the entrance to limit the number of people entering the court. Judge Xiao summoned both parties to the stand, separated them into plaintiff and defendant positions, and began the inquiry. After asking for their names, ages, birthplaces, addresses, and occupations, he immediately announced a ban on public attendance. He stated that the case involved public morals and should be closed to the public, including journalists. Therefore, the law enforcement officers and bailiffs maintaining order in the courtroom announced the court's order, requiring all those unrelated to the case to leave the courtroom. The audience withdrew like a tide. It was said that one or two people who intended to stay were persuaded to leave by the police officers. The atmosphere in the courtroom changed from tense to relaxed. However, later, some people took advantage of the judge's focus on questioning and quietly slipped back into the courtroom, standing in a corner and eavesdropping on the proceedings. The trial continued until dusk at 5:00 PM, when Judge Xiao adjourned the trial to continue on the afternoon of January 8th next year. Ji and the others then left in their cars. However, since public attendance was prohibited, the statements made by both the plaintiffs and defendants could not be learned and are omitted for now.

Tonghaili Water Cutoff Resolved 154

After negotiations, the company restored water supply

According to the New Voice News Agency, after the Tonghaili community on Tongzhou Road in Hongkou District had its main water pipe shut off by the water company on the 19th of this month, the 2,000 households were thrown into a panic. They requested the landlord, the Real Estate Department of the Land Reclamation Bank, to restore the water supply. The landlord, together with representatives of the tenants, petitioned the Public Works Department the day before yesterday. The representative He De Kui met with them and promised to relay the request to Director Zhong Shi for negotiations with the water company. After receiving the request, the water company sent staff to restore the water supply the day before yesterday (the 21st) afternoon. Yesterday's report stated that the tenants restored the water supply themselves, which is inaccurate. Yesterday, the water company sent a letter to the landlord, the Real Estate Department of the Land Reclamation Bank, stating that the water cutoff in the community was due to a misunderstanding and expressing its apologies. The water fees can also be discussed and paid through negotiations. Therefore, the water cutoff dispute in the community has been resolved. The Real Estate Association is now sending letters to its members to discuss digging artesian wells and having the water company collect the water fees directly, without the involvement of a third party, to avoid losses as before. The water fee of 7.5 yuan per 100 yuan of rent attached to the rent receipts can be deducted from the rent.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Convened a General Assembly for Public Lecture on Improving Chinese Bookkeeping 161

4 PM on the 24th

Location: Chamber of Commerce Meeting Hall

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce believes that accountant Xu Yongzuo's improved Chinese bookkeeping is a major contribution to accounting affairs in industry and commerce. It is specifically scheduled to hold a lecture on improved Chinese bookkeeping at 4 PM on the 24th of this month (i.e., Sunday) in the meeting hall, inviting accountant Xu to attend the lecture. The Chamber of Commerce has notified all trade associations in the city to inform their members of the improvements. The following is the correspondence between accountant Xu and the Chamber of Commerce:

Xu Yongzuo's letter to the Chamber of Commerce: Respected Sirs, the current bookkeeping methods in our country are broadly divided into Chinese and Western styles. Western bookkeeping, also known as new-style bookkeeping, uses horizontal writing, and relies on imported paper and ink. The accounting principles and methods are mostly confined to Western customs. Although Chinese characters can be used, numbers must be recorded in Arabic numerals. Its system and technology are too far from China's inherent habits. Not only is it difficult to imitate, but it may also make things more chaotic, and the costs are huge, neglecting the fundamentals for the sake of the trivial. Chinese bookkeeping, also known as old-style bookkeeping, uses vertical ledgers, and domestic paper and ink. The accounting principles and methods have been used for a long time, but unfortunately, the system and organization are generally lacking standards, resulting in frequent inversions and chaos. Although the cost is lower, it lacks a scientific spirit. Neither is suitable for general business circles. This accountant has served the community for many years and, lamenting the inadequacy of the current bookkeeping system, initiated a movement to improve Chinese bookkeeping. I have lectured at various universities and written articles in various journals, advocating improving Chinese bookkeeping based on our country's inherent system, adopting the latest theories in the world, and using the most economical and effective methods. The news has aroused sympathy from academic and business circles. In recent years, invitations from various schools to lecture have often been on the topic of improving Chinese bookkeeping, and commissions from various companies to design accounting systems have also been mostly on the topic of improving Chinese bookkeeping. It can be seen that improving Chinese bookkeeping has gradually moved from advocacy to implementation. Therefore, starting this year, I have devoted my spare time to designing improved Chinese bookkeeping schemes suitable for various industries and businesses. I have completed the planning and design of more than thirty types of improved Chinese accounting ledger forms, each with detailed explanations. I have also compiled a book entitled "Overview of Improved Chinese Bookkeeping" as a general explanation of the entire scheme, which has been handed over to the Standard Accounting Forms and Documents Sales Office for public sale to spread the word. Any new or old accounting staff can understand it after browsing. If there are any doubts, this office can also provide explanations. The paper is all domestic, and the records are all in Chinese characters. The savings in cost and convenience of procedures are not only far superior to Western styles but also exceed old-style bookkeeping. The detail and appropriateness of the accounting principles and methods, and the neatness and beauty of the accounting ledgers and forms, are especially unmatched by Western-style bookkeeping and old-style bookkeeping. In the contemporary accounting world, it seems to be the most economical and effective bookkeeping method. I have long admired your Chamber's leadership of the business community, and your words carry great weight. I would like to ask you to send a letter to all members, advocating its promotion, and asking various trade associations to inform various companies and firms to adopt and implement it to seek innovation in accounting matters. If you would invite me to give a public lecture at your Chamber at a set time, so that I can seek advice from experts, I would be especially grateful.

The Chamber of Commerce's reply to Xu Yongzuo: I have received your letter, stating that your book "Overview of Improved Chinese Bookkeeping" is beneficial to commercial accounting, with attached samples, and requesting that we introduce it to various industries for adoption. The Chamber has reviewed the contents of your letter. The style is detailed and practical, and it can be regarded as a major contribution to accounting. We will naturally promote it. We have scheduled an improved Chinese bookkeeping lecture at 4 PM on the 24th of this month in the meeting hall of this Chamber. At that time, we plan to invite you to attend the lecture and send additional samples of the book to the Chamber so that they can be publicly displayed for the public to browse on that day. In addition to notifying the shop members, association members, and commercial night schools in this city to inform their members to come to the meeting to listen to the lecture, we hereby reply accordingly. Please note, etc.

New Pharmaceutical Association Requests the Issuance of Flexible Certificates for Pharmacists 162

The China New Pharmaceutical Association submitted a document to the Department of Technical Health of the Ministry of Interior yesterday, stating that Article 2 of the Provisional Regulations for Pharmacists states in the second half, "Pharmacists, in addition to dispensing prescriptions from physicians, may manufacture, sell, or manage drugs." The words clearly indicate that dispensing prescriptions from physicians is the main task of pharmacists. Furthermore, Articles 11 to 16 of the same regulations provide detailed regulations for prescriptions, further proving that the previous statement is not speculation. Then the mission they bear is not as important as that of physicians. However, the qualifications stipulated in Article 3 are the same as those in Article 3 of the Provisional Regulations for Physicians. Moreover, physicians have the "Physician Flexible Certificate Issuance Measures" promulgated by the Ministry of Interior in 1932, which can be used to flexibly issue certificates, while pharmacists with a lighter mission cannot enjoy the same preferential treatment. If it is said that pharmacists have the right to manufacture prepared medicines, they can also directly put people to death. Leaving aside whether the manufacture of prepared medicines is the main task of pharmacists, even the production of a prepared medicine must comply with the provisions of Article 2 of the Regulations for the Management of Prepared Medicines, and may be sold only after submitting an application for inspection. It is far less risky than a physician who holds human life in their hands. There are only two pharmaceutical schools in the country, the private Sino-French University Pharmacy Department and the provincial Zhejiang Medical College Pharmacy Department. Each year, they train no more than 20 talents. There are also very few who study pharmacy abroad. For a country with such a vast territory as ours, it is indeed insufficient to allocate. (Omission) The Association believes that the matter concerns itself and cannot remain silent. Therefore, it has made the above statements to reach your ears. We sincerely request that you quickly issue measures for flexible certification for pharmacists.

Two Railways Improve Ticket Purchase and Luggage Transportation Procedures 163

North Station Ticket Office Open All Day for Ticket Sales

Luggage Transportation Procedures Also Improved

In order to facilitate passengers, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways have decided to open the Shanghai North Station ticket office all day starting from New Year's Day next year to sell tickets for all trains and classes on the same day, so as to avoid crowding. They will also improve luggage transportation procedures. They have ordered the Transportation and Engineering Departments to make arrangements to implement this before the fifteenth day of the first month of the lunar year. The details are recorded below:

Ticket Office Changed to Open All Day 164

The Shanghai North Station ticket office of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways has a total of 22 ticket windows. The previous regulations stipulated that certain windows were dedicated to selling tickets between certain stations. This did not cause much difficulty for literate passengers, but for illiterate passengers, these 22 windows were like looking at the ocean and sighing, unable to choose. They often did not know which stations their desired station was between, and they felt particularly distressed when asking back and forth. In order to facilitate travel, the Railway Administration has decided to adopt the following principles and measures: (1) All ticket windows at all stations on the two lines will not be limited to selling tickets for certain stations. That is, passengers can purchase tickets to any station at any window. (2) All windows will be open for ticket sales all day and night, allowing passengers to purchase tickets for any class, any train, and any station at any time. (3) Tickets sold on the same day can be used on any equivalent train on the same day. (4) Stations with more windows are allowed to differentiate sales locations by ticket class. However, in any case, the number of windows selling third and fourth-class tickets cannot be less than eight-tenths of the total. (5) Ticket sellers will not be differentiated from each other. However, for the convenience of work, they can also be handled separately according to the specific circumstances of each station. The above items have been carefully planned by the Bureau and will be implemented from January 1, 1934.

Improved Luggage Ticket Procedures 165

In addition, the procedures for handling luggage transportation at the station are not very cumbersome, but the distance between the weighing area and the ticketing area is too far, and the communication in the work is not close enough, so it takes more time, which passengers often find inconvenient. The Railway Administration plans to reorganize the luggage room at the North Station, connecting the weighing area, accounting area, ticket writing area, and ticket issuing area together. When luggage enters the station, it will be picked up by porters and taken to the weighing area for weighing. Weighing will be done immediately, regardless of whether the passenger has purchased a passenger ticket. The luggage weighing ticket will be filled out immediately after weighing. After the luggage of a passenger is weighed, the passenger will be asked which class and how many passenger tickets they have, and this information will be filled out on the ticket. The person will then sign and be responsible for the ticket. The right-hand number strip of the ticket will be torn off and given to the passenger, and the left-hand side of the ticket will be thrown to the accounting area to calculate the price. It will then be handed over to the ticket writing area to fill out the luggage ticket, and the ticket will be issued at the window based on the passenger's number strip, and the fee will be collected. The Bureau has also ordered the Transportation and Engineering Departments to quickly make arrangements to implement this before January 15, 1934.

Appeals from the Leather Tobacco Industry Association 176

The Shanghai Leather Tobacco Industry Association submitted a document to the Ministry of Finance, stating that it was submitting a report regarding the illegal collection of taxes on shredded tobacco produced from Fujian native tobacco leaves within the seven special zones. They earnestly requested a swift cessation of this practice to resolve disputes and stabilize commerce. It was found that Article 7 of the Provisional Regulations for the Collection of Special Tax on Native Tobacco, as approved by the National Government, stipulated that shredded tobacco made from native tobacco leaves for smoking would be temporarily exempt from tobacco tax. Furthermore, Article 5 of the Rules for the Inspection and Collection of Native Tobacco Leaves also stipulated that tobacco shreds were temporarily exempt from taxation in the special zones. Therefore, the association's tobacco shreds, originating from Fujian, should not be subject to taxation, regardless of whether they were imported via Xiamen or Shantou. However, the Tax Administration and the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau for Tobacco and Alcohol violated the regulations by demanding supplementary tax collection on the processed tobacco shreds, citing the lack of new tax implementation and insufficient old tax payments in Fujian Province. They did not seek tax collection at the fundamental level of native tobacco leaves. Instead, they enforced supplementary taxes on the processed shredded tobacco, establishing four provisional supplementary and refund tax measures: (1) Fujian leather tobacco shreds shipped to Shanghai between July 1, 1933, and October 31, 1933, would be subject to a special tobacco leaf tax of four yuan, one jiao, and five fen per hundred market catties, but each package (equivalent to 67 market catties) would be eligible for a two-yuan refund of the old tax. (2) Starting from November 1st of this year until the date of the special tax implementation in Fujian or the implementation of supplementary taxes in Minhou, Fujian leather tobacco shreds shipped from Shantou to Shanghai must have proof of old tax payment, and those verified would still be eligible for the tax refund under the first measure. Without proof, the new regulations for special tobacco leaf tax, charging four yuan, one jiao, and five fen per hundred market catties, would apply. (3) Shanghai was designated as the general supplementary tax zone. After supplementary tax payments in Shanghai, the goods could be transported to the mainland for retail without further inspection. In other locations, Fujian leather tobacco shreds sent via postal parcels should be subject to supplementary and refund tax payments by the local tobacco and alcohol special tax sub-bureaus based on the previous measures. (4) A tax payment certificate should be issued for both supplementary taxes paid in Shanghai and elsewhere, and the certificate should be stamped with the phrase "Tax Supplemented, Certificate Canceled" for separate filing and verification. The tobacco merchants reluctantly complied with these temporary measures. Subsequently, Zhangzhou, Fujian, implemented the special tax, and the association was preparing to request the Tax Administration to strictly implement the seventh article regarding tobacco shred tax exemption. Unexpectedly, the Tax Administration intensified its actions, using the excuse that the special tax on native tobacco leaves in Fujian Province had not yet been implemented. From December 7th, regardless of whether the goods came from Xiamen or Shantou, and whether they had new or old tax certificates, they would be treated as goods entering the special zone from non-special zones, requiring another payment of special tax. This intransigence, contradictory wording, and inconsistency made it difficult for merchants to accept. According to Article 5 of the Special Tax Regulations, Fujian Province was designated as a special tax zone. How could it be compared to non-special tax zones? Moreover, Fujian Province has already implemented the special tax, with special tax payment certificates to prove it (attached). It should not be dismissed entirely. As for the recent lack of tax revenue in Fujian Province, that is a matter of government administration and unrelated to the merchants. Furthermore, the industry has been affected by frequent banditry for years, and foreign cigarettes have severely impacted the market. The small domestic businesses are on the verge of bankruptcy, and hundreds of thousands of disaster victims in the bandit-stricken areas are about to die. If taxes are repeatedly imposed, it would be equivalent to draining the pond to catch the fish. In this time of internal and external difficulties, when the government is trying to remedy the people's livelihood, how should it alleviate the suffering of merchants, support domestic goods, and preserve them? Instead, the Tax Administration is acting in reverse, arbitrarily destroying the industry. Even if they are not considering the merchants, they should protect the tax regulations approved by the National Government. How can they act arbitrarily, disregarding the lives and deaths of merchants and treating the national tax laws as trifles? The entire association of merchants believes that this matter is critical. They cannot accept the illegal collection of tobacco shred tax. They hereby submit a report, earnestly requesting your ministry to swiftly order the Tax Administration and the Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau for Tobacco and Alcohol to cease the collection of taxes on Fujian tobacco shreds within the special zones to resolve disputes and stabilize commerce. We await your urgent order. Respectfully submitted to Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance. (Attached: Special Tax Payment Certificate for Native Tobacco Leaves from Zhangzhou, Fujian). Respectfully submitted by Lai Zhenhuan, Lu Yunwu, and Jiang Buyun of the Shanghai Leather Tobacco Industry Association.

A Young Woman Loses Her Virginity After a Movie and a Banquet 182

Only After Cohabitation Does She Discover Her Husband Has a Wife

Now Being Prosecuted for Bigamy and Assault

Wu Dai, an elderly woman from Changzhou, is 72 years old and lives in the countryside. She has a son and a daughter. Her son, Jingxiu, is a businessman in Shanghai. Her daughter, Suzhen, is 32 years old and of modest beauty. She married Chen Zicheng, a fellow villager. In the autumn of this year, she came to Shanghai to find work as a factory worker and stayed with Shen Meiying, a fellow villager, in the French Concession. Shen is living with Zhang Huaifu, also known as Zhang Laoer, a local man. Zhang works in a flower shop and is friends with Chen Jinding (44 years old), who is in the same industry. Chen operates his own Yunlong Flower Shop at No. 45, the intersection of Avenue du Père Froc and Route de Say Zoong in the French Concession. He has a wife and family in the countryside who take care of the farmland. Because Chen lives alone in Shanghai, he is looking for a companion to alleviate his loneliness as a traveler. He often visits Zhang's house and becomes acquainted with Suzhen. On the afternoon of September 6, Shen Meiying and Zhang Huaifu invited Suzhen to watch a movie at the Empire Theater on Avenue Joffre. Chen was also at the theater and met Shen, Zhang, and Suzhen. Chen thought Suzhen was attractive and developed affection for her. After the movie, Chen invited Shen, Zhang, Suzhen, and others to a friend's house nearby for a rest. They went to the Tiansheng Hotel in Baixianqiao. They entered through the back door, booked a room, and colluded with Shen and Zhang to order wine and dishes to entertain Suzhen. Suzhen was unsuspecting and fell into their trap. After getting her drunk, Shen and Zhang left together. Chen then had sexual intercourse with Suzhen overnight. Afterward, Chen told Suzhen that he had no wife and asked her to marry him and live together. He also wrote a note for Suzhen, stating that if he abandoned her or committed bigamy, he would be responsible for her support. Suzhen was still hesitating when her husband learned of the matter in Shanghai and immediately wrote an agreement to divorce Suzhen. At this point, Suzhen had nowhere to go, and what was done was done, so she accepted Chen's proposal. On October 28, the two held a wedding ceremony at the Hexinglou Restaurant on Chongqing Road, with Wang Changfa as the witness. After the marriage and cohabitation began, Chen often told Suzhen that he had a wife in Shanghai and a concubine at home. Suzhen thought he was joking, but she recently learned that Chen did indeed have a wife at home. She confronted Chen, but he beat her. He then abandoned her and did not provide for her daily expenses. Suzhen believed that Chen's behavior was so violent and that he had colluded to deceive her into marriage. She could not live with him and grow old together. She informed her brother, Jingxiu, who sent for their elderly mother, Dai, to come to Shanghai. They hired lawyers Xu Wu and Zhang Deyou to file a criminal complaint against Chen and Shen Meiying and Zhang Huaifu in the Second Special District Court for fraud, bigamy, and assault, requesting imprisonment, and also filed a civil suit to recover 10,140 yuan in alimony, calculated at 30 yuan per month for 28 years and two months. Wang Zuifa was called as a witness. After the court received the complaint and served it, the defendant, Chen Jinding, hired lawyer Shen Yiqian to defend him. He submitted a response and filed a counterclaim against Wu Suzhen, Wu Jingxiu, and Wu Dai for colluding to frame him. He stated that in July of this year, the defendant hosted a Mid-Autumn Festival banquet at home and invited guests. Suzhen and Zhang Huaifu came to eat and became acquainted. Suzhen knew that the defendant had a wife. Suzhen's brother, Jingxiu, said that Suzhen was having difficulty with food and clothing and was willing to be the defendant's concubine. After Jingxiu discussed the matter at the hotel, they rented No. 102 Pushi Road and lived together. Jingxiu also said that they had to hold a banquet to save face. Jingxiu wrote a draft invitation and printed it, but the defendant could not read and did not understand that he had written "remarriage" on the invitation, intending to blackmail him. No wedding ceremony was held at Hexinglou. After cohabitation, he bought Suzhen clothes and accessories worth more than 180 yuan. Jingxiu also borrowed 60 yuan. On October 7, Suzhen took the clothes and left without saying goodbye. She came back on the 9th. After the defendant scolded Suzhen, she reported him to the police for assault. The police did not accept the case. She also colluded with her mother to file a complaint. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu Fanglian summoned both parties and witnesses to the Criminal Court No. 2 for questioning and instructed them to wait for a later date for further questioning.

Garden Villa Robbery Case Solved 189

On September 22 of this year, four robbers broke into the home of Huang Shaocen, a Cantonese man living at No. 33 Garden Villa, Route de Say Zoong in the French Concession. They spoke Cantonese and threatened him with guns. As a result, two diamond rings, two jeweled rings, clothing, and cash were stolen, with an estimated loss of about six or seven thousand yuan. The robbers then left. After the incident, the victim reported it to the Lujiawan Police Station. Several months passed, and there was no trace of the robbers. Police Inspector Jin Jiulin recently received a tip that the robbers in the case were hiding in Hongkou. He personally led Detective Zhang Ziying, Qian Yimin, and other detectives to Hongkou at 6:00 a.m. yesterday. They met with the Hongkou detectives and waited at the entrance of Tianfu Lane, Bazili Road. Soon, they saw a man walking out of the lane. The informant confirmed that he was the man. He was arrested on the spot. He confessed that he was a Cantonese man named Qu Shude, 30 years old, and admitted to the robbery. A letter of appointment was found on him, stating that he was a staff officer and aviator of the First Route Headquarters. Three pawn tickets and a machine cover were also found. He was immediately taken back to the police station and sent to the Second Court for interrogation this morning.

At the Yongyuan Silk Dyeing Factory at No. 20 Wei Wu Zhi Road, Xiejiao Xujiang Road, a fire broke out suddenly due to a short circuit at around 5:00 p.m. yesterday. Fortunately, it did not spread to the neighboring houses. It is reported that the factory has been operating for many years and is substantial. The factory buildings, inventory, and raw materials that were burned were worth about 30,000 yuan. Soybean and Rice Industry Adds a Wharf 192

The Soybean and Rice Industry Association stated that in the past two years, the amount of rice shipped from various producing areas to Shanghai has been extremely prosperous. The rice all comes from boatmen, and the arriving rice boats dock at the association's own wharf to unload. The wharf was originally intended for rice boats to dock and unload, but in recent years, boats carrying miscellaneous grains and oil cakes have also docked there because the loading and unloading is convenient, resulting in a lack of docking space on the wharf. Disputes often occur as boats compete to unload. The association stated that the miscellaneous grains and oil cake boats also belong to the association's members, so they have added a wharf to the north of the original Xuejiajia wharf and have built a three-story steel-concrete warehouse along the bank, specifically to store soybeans, rice, and miscellaneous grains, so that the cargo ships can unload as soon as they arrive, avoiding congestion. The added wharf is currently being designed and implemented. The warehouse was contracted by the Jiuji Construction Company this spring and is being built day and night. It has now been completed. The opening ceremony was held the other day. The association invited various groups to visit and provided refreshments, hosted by Chairman Gu Xinyi, Standing Committee Member Chen Ziyi, Cai Yukun, and others. Storage has already begun, with soybeans and rice being the most stored.

Spring and Autumn

Export 201

— Hua Ling

When China is mentioned, one invariably and naturally thinks of its vast territory and abundant resources. Although the four northeastern provinces are no longer ours, when China is mentioned, one still inevitably thinks of its vast territory and abundant resources.

Speaking of vast territory and abundant resources, I find it very contradictory. According to customs reports, since the establishment of customs, there has not been a single year in which exports exceeded imports. Whether it is food, drink, clothing, daily necessities, reading materials, viewing materials, transportation, or various industrial raw materials, we all rely on imported goods. From this, we should slap ourselves in the face and ask: "Are resources abundant?"

In such a large China, the only things that are shipped overseas, to put it bluntly, are "silk" and "tea." Let's not even talk about the decline of the silk and tea trade in recent years. Even during the peak sales period, there was never any direct trade with foreign markets. It was just doing some small-scale business with the import and export foreign firms stationed in China. If foreign merchants did not come to China to do this trading business, it would be pitiful. Although China has a vast territory and abundant resources, the world markets might not have discovered Chinese silk and tea.

This is not the author exaggerating; it is indeed the case. To put it more bluntly, there are many more examples. If foreign ships did not play the trick of bringing in yellow croaker, there would definitely not be so many Qingtian peddlers in Europe today. If Western missionaries had not introduced the Chinese golden lotus and pigtails, etc., the civilization of the ancient oriental country to the world, perhaps Westerners would still not be familiar with the situation in China. Everyone, please think about it. These things cannot be directly exported by ourselves and have to rely on others. How can we talk about formal commodities?

However, recently there is a plan for "Chinese fruits to be directly shipped overseas." Wonderful! This may be due to entering the next Yuan cycle, so we can finally raise our heads and start the first record of Chinese exports. This is naturally a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity. How can I not be overjoyed? However, I hope that the fruit merchants will work hard to open up a direct export route for China, with its vast territory and abundant resources, and not allow foreign consumers to confirm that "these are products of an inferior nation." Otherwise, alas, I can't bear to say it.

"Filial Sons Come from Under the Stick" 202

— Xu Haowu

Ever since Washington Irving said, "Spare the rod and spoil the child," the Chinese "philosophers" who have always advocated "filial sons come from under the stick" can "quote the classics" and say arrogantly: "I am not alone!"

Indeed, young children are ignorant and easily indulge their emotions. As parents, standing in the position of nurturing and supervising, they should strictly guide and restrain them to fulfill their responsibilities as parents. However, the reality is often "off-topic."

I have personally seen a little girl. Her tattered clothes, sallow skin, thin muscles, and swollen face, needless to say, at a glance, one knows that she was not born to enjoy the blessings of wealthy parents. Often her little cheeks are puffed up, her little lips are closed, and her little eyebrows are slightly furrowed. She can sit there for several hours without moving or making a sound. Unless someone asks her, she will answer a word or two. If you ask her to move around, I can't say she doesn't move. Hey! How can she not move? However, her feet move and her hands sway, always slowly, mechanically, and weakly. Don't say lively and innocent, even the minimum of liveliness is really hard to find!

People say to me behind my back: "Her parents are really fierce! Saying too much will get you beaten; not listening will get you beaten; even if nothing is wrong, they will lose their temper and beat her! Beat! Beat! Beat!"

Thinking carefully, her mother is still her biological mother. Feeling pain for her own flesh, she may sometimes have regrets. What about those poor children who lost their mothers early and live under the tyrannical power of their stepmothers all day long? Wearing a reed flower padded jacket, which seems so light, soft, and thick to outsiders, and the stepmother seems so gentle and loving; in reality? Enduring sorrow and bitterness, swallowing tears. There is no shortage of people who have experienced it firsthand, so why should I, who have not experienced it, "scratch the itch from outside the boot?"

The problem here is no longer whether the family circumstances are spacious or not. The reality is like this, and the customs have continued like this. Otherwise, it would not be a "famous" "stepmother"!

Let me put aside those virtuous parents who are ignorant of indulgence. Even those parents who use "restraint" to whip and beat, and use whipping and beating to bury their children's happiness, extinguish their children's innocence, shackle their children's freedom, and deeply engrave the images of human cruelty, violence, and viciousness on their pure little hearts, thus leaving the root of misanthropy, although their heart of cultivating "filial sons" is commendable, I am afraid there will be some criticism ("There are no wrong parents in the world," crazy words deserve a beating!). Fortunately, there is still "legacy" to follow!

Special Goodnight 204

— Rong Yu

"Wish you a good night!" Although this is a common polite greeting, when the other person puts on a kind smile and speaks in a gentle tone, you will not feel completely comfortable, but you will certainly not be disgusted. Because when he says good night to you, it always contains some respect.

However, people who live in Shanghai have another special goodnight, please accept it. This kind of goodnight is hideous, rude, and also requires you to pay a considerable price to them.

The big clock at the customs struck two o'clock. At this time, the road was quiet, with only a few rickshaws dragging along listlessly, and the food stalls flickering with phosphorescent lights. The wealthy gentlemen and ladies were either just finishing their drunken songs or returning from dancing. If you took a motorcycle or lived in a lively area, of course, there would be no accidents on the way back. But if you took a rickshaw or walked, and your home was on a remote road, in this cold wind and dim light, a few burly men would jump out from the side and block your way. They would point a shiny black pistol at your vitals and say, "Hey! Friend, be sensible, don't make a sound!"

If you are a beautiful friend, let them do as they please, confiscate your purse, and take off your clothes. Let them leave triumphantly, and you can only admit your bad luck. If you are not sensible and shout loudly, before the detectives arrive, you will be beaten, which is not worth it. So, when you meet someone who says a special goodnight to you, you can only accept it obediently and pay the price quickly. Other than that, what other way is there to think of?

One day, my relative, Mr. So-and-so, also encountered someone saying a special goodnight. Because he didn't have any money with him, the few people who said goodnight were very frustrated. In addition to confiscating his clothes, they also stripped off his shiny leather shoes, forcing him to walk home in his socks.

Another time, two female guests were taking a rickshaw home when they also encountered a few people saying goodnight on the way. They also knew that "men and women are different" and did not search them. One didn't have any cash, so she lost a wool coat. The other lost a handbag containing a dozen silver dollars. Afterwards, they said, "If these people who said goodnight had searched them carefully, they would have found dozens of yuan in banknotes in their tight-fitting pockets!"

"Stripping the pig." Imagine encountering such thugs on the road. In addition to losing clothes and money, you also have to endure abuse. Isn't that a double loss? So I propose that the phrase "stripping the pig" be abolished. Anyone who has received this kind of blessing will definitely agree!

Four Company Commanders in the Northeast 205

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 20: The Old Man Smiles for Days at a Fortunate Date, The Old Friends Live Across the Street and Their Worries are Endless

He sacrificed a lot for me, and he even swore that he would not return to his brother's house until he made a fortune. Now that he hasn't made a fortune, why has he returned to his brother's house? Could it be that this is also for my sake? If this is also for my sake, what can I use to comfort him? It's so embarrassing to see him. It would be boring to comfort him with a few nice words, and it would also raise a lot of suspicion. Furthermore, even if I comfort him, telling him not to take me to heart, it seems to me that it would be better not to comfort him at all. If I did comfort him, I'm afraid he would miss me even more. With this thought, Guizhi decided to ignore Second Master Gan. When it was time to sleep at night, she remembered that there was a photo of Ji Zhi in her pillowcase. This thing, keeping it by her side, would cause trouble sooner or later, and it would always cause trouble, disturbing her thoughts. It would be better to put it in a place where she would never see it. But after her mother fell asleep, when she touched the photo, it was not in the pillowcase, but on the mattress, covered by the pillow. She remembered clearly that she had put it in the pillowcase, so why had it changed places? Could it be that her mother had seen it? If her mother had seen it, it would show that she still had divided loyalties. Her mother was a conservative person, so she would look down on her even more. At that time, there were no lights in the room, and she didn't dare to light a fire. In the dark, she threw the photo into the crack in the kang, planning to wait until her mother was not at home to find a proper place to store it. That night, with this heavy thought added to her mind, she tossed and turned and couldn't sleep. Naturally, she woke up even later the next day. When she opened her eyes, she saw her mother with a cigarette in her mouth, sitting diagonally on a square stool by the door. Her mother was a non-smoker, which she knew. This was also extremely uncomfortable in her heart, so she was smoking there to relieve boredom and think about things. This might have something to do with the photo under the pillow? (275)

Shanghai Newspaper Wireless Radio Weekly

The Importance of Modulation 206

— Shi Huayu

Why do we need to pay attention to the modulation when listening to distant broadcasting stations? It turns out that the loudness of the sound received from distant radio stations is greatly related to the modulation component. Because the loudness is directly proportional to the square of the electric field strength and the modulation. Now let L represent the original loudness, F be the electric field strength, and M be the modulation, then the formula is as follows:

F² × M = L

For example, when we receive a distant radio station, its modulation is assumed to be 33⅓%. When receiving another distant radio station, the modulation is 66⅔%. If the power of the two radio stations is equal, then the sound we receive from the former is only half as loud as the latter. Therefore, we can see from the above formula that the loudness of the sound received from distant radio stations is indeed related to its power, but the modulation is also very important, and modulation is even more important than power! Because only the square of F is directly proportional to L.

Now suppose there are two distant radio stations A and B. The F of radio station A is 0.002 volts per meter (Millivolt/Meter), and the modulation is 50%. The F of radio station B is 0.0015 volts per meter, and M = 80%. What is the ratio of the sound loudness we receive? It is very easy to calculate according to the above formula.

Radio Station A: 0.002² × 0.5 = 0.000002

Radio Station B: 0.0015² × 0.8 = 0.0000018

The ratio of L is 0.0000024 : 0.0000018 = 4 : 3

For example, the F of radio station C is 0.0007 volts per meter, and the modulation is 100%; the E of radio station D is 0.0005 volts per meter, and the modulation is 50%. Then,

Radio Station C: 0.0007² × 1.0 = 0.00000049

Radio Station D: 0.0005² × 0.5 = 0.000000125

The ratio of F of the two radio stations is 7:5, and the ratio of L is 4:1. The two ratios obtained above show the reason why modulation is more important than power. Therefore, if the modulation percentage of a powerful radio station is not enough, although the power is strong, it will not have good results.

Calculation of Triode Power Output and Distortion 208

— Yizhi

The power output and distortion of a triode cannot exceed its characteristic fixed value, otherwise the sound reproduction will be blurred. Therefore, when using a triode for amplification, its output power and distortion should be calculated first to avoid excessive output and distortion. Now, each vacuum tube manufacturer attaches its characteristic table to the vacuum tube sold for inspection, which can save calculation. However, we should know its calculation method. If the power output and distortion of the vacuum tube are not noted, we can calculate to obtain it.

When the gate of the vacuum tube is stimulated by the AC peak voltage of the input signal, if it is a positive half-wave, it will be equal to zero from the gate position; if it is stimulated by a negative half-wave, it will become twice the original value from the gate position. Therefore, gate voltage stimulation indicates the maximum and minimum voltages and currents. The power output can be calculated using the following formula:

Power Output = (Maximum Current - Minimum Current) × (Maximum Current - Minimum Current) ÷ 8

The percentage of second harmonic distortion can be calculated using the following formula:

Second Harmonic Distortion = (Maximum Current + Minimum Current - Load Current) ÷ 2 ÷ (Maximum Current - Minimum Current) × 100

For example: The screen voltage of a certain triode is 250 volts, the screen current is 34 milliamps, the gate voltage is 50 volts, and the load resistance is 3900 ohms. The characteristic curve of its screen voltage and screen current EP IP is shown in the figure. Find its power output and distortion value.

Solution: Draw a straight line Xy parallel to AB through point P in the figure (that is, the intersection of the gate voltage 50 volts and the screen voltage 250 volts should have a current of 34 milliamps). The AB line is drawn between points M and O. Point M is the intersection of the screen voltage 250 volts and the screen current zero amps. Point Q is the intersection of the screen voltage zero volts and the screen current is equal to the quotient obtained by dividing the screen voltage 250 volts by the screen resistance of 3900 ohms. The quotient is: 25 ÷ 390 = 0.064 amps, which can be used to calculate the following formula:

Power Output = (0.066 - 0.007) × (0.066 - 0.007) ÷ 8 = 0.000434925 Watts

The harmonic distortion can be obtained by the formula:

Second Harmonic Distortion = (0.066 + 0.007 - (2 ÷ 0.066 - 0.007)) × 100 = 4.2%

The distortion of the vacuum tube must not exceed 5%, and its load resistance at the best operating point is about twice the screen resistance. These two problems are very important on the vacuum tube, so they are attached.

The Ratio of Electricity to Volume丨The Meaning of Decibel丨 209

— Li Yuanqing

Calculating the relationship between two ordinary objects is generally very simple. For example, if one battery costs one yuan, then two yuan can buy two batteries, and five yuan can buy five batteries… In short, spending a certain amount of money buys the same amount of batteries. This kind of regular change is called a linear ratio in mathematics.

However, in radio, the relationship between volume and electricity is not so simple. For example, if the power of a radio is increased by half, the change in output volume is almost imperceptible to the average person. Doubling the power of a radio only results in a slight change in volume. In fact, it takes four times the power of a radio to achieve twice the volume.

We know that sound waves are produced by the vibration of objects. A larger vibration force results in larger sound waves, and a smaller vibration force results in smaller sound waves. However, the change in the magnitude of the vibration force and the strength of the sound waves is irregular — it is not a linear ratio, but a logarithmic ratio.

The method commonly used to calculate the ratio of electricity to volume is the Bel system. In the Bel system, a tenfold increase in electricity corresponds to a one Bel increase in volume. However, in radio engineering, it is rare to increase electricity by a factor of ten or a hundred, so one Bel is too large for practical use. Therefore, one Bel is divided into ten smaller Bels — each smaller Bel (Decibel) is equal to one-tenth of a Bel.

According to the ordinary situation, ten times the electricity can get ten decibels (that is, one Bel), then, four times the electricity can only get four decibels; two times the electricity, can only get two decibels. But in fact, it is not like this!

As mentioned above, the relationship between electricity and volume is a logarithmic ratio. Thus, it is known that the Bel changes according to the logarithm of the "power multiple." Expressed as a formula, it is: Bel 10gP1 - P2

Decibel 10 10gP1P2 (P1 first power) (P2 second power)

For example, if the output power of a radio is originally 200 milliwatts (P1), and is now increased to 400 milliwatts (P2), according to the above formula, we get:

Decibel = 10 10g400 - 200 = 10 10g2 = 10X.3 = 3 (To be continued)

Small Experience

Another Use for Bypass Capacitors 210

— Zhu Ziyuan

I once assembled a three-circuit single-tube radio, using an R.C.A.-30 tube, a B battery of 45 volts, and adjusting the feedback force with a variable feedback coil. Because I felt the effect was already good, I did not install a bypass capacitor. Unexpectedly, when listening with headphones, touching the headphone wires would cause a loud squeal, and the same problem would occur when a person approached. Later, I had to connect a 0.002 fixed capacitor between the headphone end of the feedback coil and A-B, and connect A-B to ground. This problem was completely resolved, the feedback force was greatly strengthened, and the sound quality was clearer. If the adjustment of the feedback force is not stable when using the feedback coil, then the 0.002 fixed capacitor can be replaced with a 0.00025 variable capacitor, and the problem can be avoided. The adjustment of regeneration will be much smoother.

About Materials for Self-Made Power Transformers 211

— Lu Qing

If you don't use specially made silicon steel sheets with high permeability to make a power transformer, you can use good, flat wrought iron sheets (because wrought iron also has very high permeability). Cut them into a 日 shape, and then coat them with shellac (i.e., shellac dissolved in alcohol, which is sold in paint stores or instrument shops). This thinned solution reduces eddy current loss and can be used as the core, with very good results.

After the opening ceremony,

▲He Siyuan delivered a speech, roughly saying that the discussion at today's conference of principals will focus on the following three points: first, how normal school students can serve; second, how to train them; and third, how to examine them. We know that in the past, service was limited to schools, because in the past (Qing Dynasty), there were limited numbers of Xiucai and Juren, which restricted education. Now the purpose of education is universal education. However, although the current system has changed, the students' mentality of seeking education and making a fortune still exists, and society's expectations have not changed, still clinging to the gentry concept. In today's society, we should especially move towards productive education and survival education. All of this should start with normal school education. The old concept of simply eliminating illiteracy is not a fundamental solution, because literacy is only a tool, not the goal. Having knowledge does not necessarily mean being literate. Primary school teachers should first understand the students' families and second, implement adult education (not necessarily literacy). Third, according to Professor Buck's investigation of Chinese farmers, they have eight months of slack time each year, so the mission of rural primary school teachers should be to enable farmers to engage in handicrafts as a side business, encourage farmers to weave cloth and make hand-rolled cigarettes, etc., and order each county to restrict the sale of paper cigarettes (except for self-made ones). Other various cooperative methods can be used to induce them to do so. For example, teach weaving and then recognize the character "cloth," teach cigarette making and then recognize the character "cigarette," etc. In this way, we can start from the economic aspect and literacy, so that they know that education is life, not just literacy. If the above three methods are followed, how should we train normal school students to make them suitable? Only with this condition can we have universal education, not restricted education. However, this matter does not necessarily have to be done throughout the province, starting with one county or one school is also possible. Therefore, normal school students should be issued a temporary certificate in addition to the courses that can be examined. After they work, their work performance should be evaluated before they are given a graduation certificate. Therefore, we should decide how to train normal school students in order to decide how to examine them. I hope everyone will come up with a concrete plan.

▲Discussion by Principals After the speech, the principals expressed their opinions and discussed together in order to first formulate a concrete plan regarding the service, training, and examination of normal school students, and then discuss the examination issues. After a long discussion, because there were too many people and the speeches filled the hall, it was difficult to come up with a unified outline. Therefore, it was decided to switch to group discussions, and the chairman appointed five people to serve as group leaders, each leading a discussion. Those designated were Cai Fuyuan, principal of the First Normal School, Yang Shutian, principal of the Second Normal School, Qian Zhendong, principal of the First Rural Normal School, Zhao Derou, principal of the Fourth Rural Normal School, and Wang Xuxing, principal of Qihe County Normal School. The City Children's Welfare Association Actively Prepares for Children's Year 222

▲Opening Program for New Year's Day Next Year Has Been Scheduled

▲Mayor's Reception for Children to be Held in Mid-January

▲The Standing Committee Meeting Will Be Held at the Lianchou Society at 3:00 PM Today

The City Education, Social Affairs, Health, and Public Safety Bureaus, in view of the urgent need to develop children's affairs in the city, established the City Children's Welfare Committee in early September of this year, in order to promote social attention to the status of children, develop children's affairs, and seek the welfare of children throughout the city. The association also decided to designate next year as Children's Year, in order to awaken social attention to children, and is actively preparing. The preparations are described below:

Preparation Situation The association drafted a proposal to designate next year as Children's Year, which was jointly submitted to the City Government and the City Social Affairs Bureau for approval through the China Child Welfare Association. It has been approved and the organizational outline of the Children's Year Committee was adopted at the fourth standing committee meeting, and the committee members of each group of Children's Year and various publicity methods were also appointed. The appointment letters for the Children's Year Committee members have been submitted to the Mayor for issuance. The various publicity methods are currently being rushed, and all can be realized on New Year's Day of Children's Year.

Reception for Children The association originally planned to invite Mayor Wu to receive children from all countries in the city on New Year's Day, but because the City Government is currently moving and the Mayor also has to receive foreign guests on that day, it is feared that he will not have time to take care of both. Therefore, it has been decided to schedule the reception in mid-January to promote it.

Opening Program The program for the opening day of Children's Year is as follows: (1) Mayor regularly meets with children from the city and all countries; (2) Negotiate with cinemas to invite children to watch movies; (3) Mayor, Director of Social Affairs, and Director of Education give speeches on Fuxing Radio Station; (4) Request the Health Bureau to find a way for hospitals to provide free health checks for children; (5) Request major newspapers to publish special editions for Children's Year; (6) Post slogans for Children's Year throughout the city; (7) Various children's books, newspapers, and pictures publish special editions for Children's Year; (8) All parks are open; (9) The Home Industry Society Children's Dental Clinic officially opens and offers free check-up coupons; (10) Request major companies to set up special children's goods departments; (11) All hospitals open free physical examinations and free treatment for children; (12) Mayor gives children gifts (Children's Shanghai Sightseeing Game Park is compiled and printed by the Shanghai Children's Welfare Association and Children's Morning Post); (13) Children's domestic product gifts; (14) Film the opening film for Children's Year; (15) Hold a toy exhibition; (16) Hold a children's carnival.

Children's Gifts If major factories are willing to donate gifts for the opening of Children's Year, please contact Dao Shengjun of the Citizens Promoting Domestic Goods Association (telephone 91069), or Wu Tanhao of the Shanghai Domestic Goods Company, or Hu Xiyuan of the Yabu Er Electric Bulb Factory. Bookstores that are willing to donate children's books can contact Hu Shuyi of the City Education Bureau.

Today's Standing Committee Meeting In order to actively carry out Children's Year, the association has scheduled a tea party at the Shanghai Lianhuan Association of the Silk Industry Bank on Sanma Road at 3:00 PM today (Saturday). The tea party will be hosted by Pan Gongzhan, chairman of the standing committee, and members of each group of the standing committee of Children's Year, and all plans for the Children's Year will be discussed.

Municipal Stadium Decided to be Built in the City Center 238

Occupying an Area of Approximately 300 Mu

Construction Cost: 1 Million Yuan

Shanghai Mayor Wu Tiecheng previously convened prominent figures from Shanghai's elite circles and the business community to discuss the city's library, museum, and stadium. Preparatory meetings have been held repeatedly. According to city government sources, the locations of the museum and library have not yet been determined. However, the stadium has been decided to be built in the city center, utilizing existing parkland within the area, expanding and transforming it. It will occupy an area of approximately 300 mu, with a construction cost of 1 million yuan. The mayor has hired several experts to handle the planning. Once the city government has completely moved to the city center, construction will begin. It is hoped that the Second National Games of the Republic of China in 1935 and the next Far Eastern Games can be held in the new stadium, it is said.

Jian De Defeats Ze Xin 6-1 in Xiangbin Cup Final 239

The final of the 6th Xiangbin Cup table tennis tournament was held as scheduled at the Ningbo Fellow Villagers Association the night before. The strength of the Jian De and Ze Xin teams was considered to be equal. Unexpectedly, the result of the competition was that Ze Xin was miserably defeated by a score of 1 to 6. Looking back on the competition, Ze Xin's defeat was truly due to a lack of spirit and courage. The loss of the third group by a score of 1 to 3 was the most fatal blow. Afterwards, the team's morale was greatly disrupted, and they had no fighting spirit at all. Jian De, on the other hand, was filled with heroic spirit, and the soldiers gave their all. As a result, they won three more groups. Ze Xin was miserably defeated. In the final group, the Jian De team members forfeited. The audience suddenly began to criticize. For a moment, the order was slightly disrupted. Fortunately, the officials of the cup tournament invited Jian De's Lu Xiulu and Ze Xin's Deng Guofu to give a demonstration match to calm things down.
