Page 17

Free Talk

The Great Wall 241

— Xi

China’s Great Wall is, like the Egyptian pyramids, one of the world's famous, great, and ancient structures. Recently, the historian Hendrik Willem van Loon described the Great Wall of China in his works, saying: "... along the Yellow Sea coast, the fertile plains of China were always open to the strong invaders of Central Asia. To compensate for this shortcoming, the Chinese emperors of the third century BC built a huge city wall, 1,500 miles long, 20 feet wide, and more than 30 feet high, from Liaodong Bay all the way to the Jiayu Pass west of Yizhou City on the edge of the Gobi Desert. This granite barrier has served its purpose well. In the middle of the seventeenth century, the Manchus attacked fiercely, but it could not resist. However, a defense that has lasted for nearly two thousand years is, after all, no small matter. The walls we build today will be useless after ten years, and we will have to spend a great deal of money to rebuild them. ..." I can't tell if this is praise or mockery. However, the Great Wall did its duty in protecting the territory and ensuring the safety of the people from the Han Dynasty to before the Qing Dynasty. Who says that from the Han Dynasty to now, every scholar has scolded Qin Shihuang? But we should speak up for Qin Shihuang on this point. If it weren’t for this autocratic tyrant building this huge city wall to block the invasion of the Huns, perhaps the Huns would have already moved south to graze their horses, and we would not have been able to study the Four Books for thousands of years.

Since China’s territory expanded north to the Sayan Mountains, the Great Wall has become something only for sightseeing and appreciation. Although it seemed to have done a little duty for both sides in the Zhili-Fengtian War, this was a small matter for the Chinese themselves and not worth mentioning. In short, the Great Wall has indeed been dead for hundreds of years.

However, things in the world are unpredictable. The Great Wall, which had been dead for hundreds of years, has been resurrected after some ingenious changes one after another since the September 18th Incident in Shenyang. Not only is it serving us, but it is also serving our invaders. This kind of miracle of "turning decay into magic" is something that not even the autocratic tyrant Qin Shihuang, who lived twenty years ago, could have foreseen, nor could the modern geographer Hendrik Willem van Loon have foreseen. Van Loon praised it as a defense that has lasted for more than two thousand years, but we still don’t know how many more years it will last! Thinking of this, I really can't help but join Van Loon in praising it as "no small matter after all"!

In a Small Opium Shop 242

— Li Huiying

A friend led me into a small opium shop in "Manchukuo." Its name was "Drunken Immortals Abode."

The time was at night. As soon as I entered, I felt as if I had entered another world. In this world, there is no bright sun, no fresh air. What it has is a strong, stimulating fragrance, and some dim lights that appear and disappear in the hazy smoke. This is probably the blessed land where the immortals lie drunk. I congratulated myself for also becoming an immortal once.

A large room with plank beds built facing each other. The beds on both sides were full of people. Small opium lamps, fragrant smoke, and the "che la," "che la" sound of smoking drove all the people toward the land of immortals.

"Come on, old man."

Like a waiter in a restaurant, a waiter with a smoke tray in his hand greeted us and then pointed to one of the few remaining empty spaces on the big bed.

Fortunately, he called me back to the human world, and all the phenomena in front of me escaped from the land of immortals.

My friend, a man who had been mixing in the world of Harbin for many years, had considerable experience in social matters. He stood motionless on the floor, only glancing sideways with his eyes. This had an effect. Sure enough, the waiter changed his tune:

"Ah, do you gentlemen want to go to a private room?"

After asking this question, before we could even nod our heads, he shouted:

"A private room for two!"

Stepping out of the big room, I followed my friend to the backyard, where the private rooms were located. Each one was a small, single room. At first glance, it was no different from the setup of a restaurant. I never thought that a small shop would have different seating arrangements and such a large scale.

However, I was startled by a strange laughter from a woman, and I quietly asked my friend:

"What? Are there women here?"

"No, you'll find out in a while."

After he finished speaking, I accompanied him to lie down on the plank bed in the private room. The small plank bed could only accommodate the two of us, with only room for the opium lamp in the middle. The waiter came over, took out two opium bubbles, and said with a smile:

"Gentlemen, would you like to call one to play?"

My friend looked at me and smiled. I understood what his smile meant. He was answering the question I had just asked him. I realized that the women here were prostitutes.

"What do you think?"

He asked for my opinion, and I shook my head.

This made him laugh:

"Old friend, you've been traveling south and north for so many years, and you haven't learned any good tricks. You have to call one, you absolutely have to call one."

He sent the waiter away. I didn't say anything more. Anyway, I was here for sightseeing. Seeing more is naturally better than seeing nothing. However, to be honest, I am really incompetent in these kinds of situations, and I even blush at the mention of them.

I watched my friend smoke. Because I had agreed with him beforehand that I would absolutely not take a single puff, he lit the opium and smoked it himself, without offering it to me. I watched him smoke, the smoke puffing out one puff at a time. Suddenly, I felt that this matter was very poetic. From burning the opium, to inhaling it into the stomach, and then exhaling the remaining smoke, this requires considerable artistic cultivation. However, when I thought of how this one gun could ruin a person’s life, and how the current "Manchukuo," under the direction of Japanese imperialism, was using the public sale of opium to eliminate the Manchurian people's ambition and courage to resist, all the poetry I felt was dispelled, and the drifting smoke was like a layer of impenetrable clouds of sorrow for me.

When the woman revealed her sallow face at the door, I stood up and said goodbye to my friend. I said to him:

"Friend, I can't do it. I'm feeling a little unwell, I have a headache, let me go back first."

Nalan Chengde's Poetic Theory (Continued) 243

— Chen Liang

Six

In addition, Nalan Chengde also studied phonetics, the origins of poetry, and other topics, which cannot all be introduced here. However, from what has already been discussed, we can know that he was a scholar with broad knowledge and in-depth research. His success, as evidenced by "Lushui Ting Miscellaneous Records," comes more from diligent learning than from genius. This is something very worthy of our attention, something that we cannot think of simply by reading his poems. In this book, there is also a point that, although it discusses other matters, his view that one must first understand the spirit of others before criticizing them is extremely valuable. Many scholars today (?) often criticize people without first trying to understand their scholarship. I think Nalan Chengde's opinion is also very beneficial for them. In these two senses, I will quote this passage as the conclusion of this article:

If you do not read their books and do not know their ways, but only hold onto your own opinions and scold them recklessly, you will only reveal your own ignorance... Generally speaking, when people of the same school gather together, they can only talk about the things of their own school. They consider themselves outstanding, but they do not realize their own ignorance. In reading, it is important to be meticulous; in learning, it is important to be broad and practical. Speaking and writing, galloping a horse cannot catch up. It is not an easy task.

Small Notes from a Traveler's Window 244

— Shu

Sixteen

Lu You's "Lao Xue An Notes" records:

When Liu Shaomei was in the capital, he did not travel with his family for many years. He used his salary exclusively to copy books. He would copy each book three times, even if it was a work of hundreds of volumes. When he was not working, he would close his door and proofread the books, not receiving guests. After returning to Sichuan, he divided the books into three boats to guard against loss. Later, when traveling to Zigui Xintan, one boat was destroyed by the rocks of the rapids. The other two boats were unharmed, so he returned to Puci and built a pavilion to store them.

Liu Shaomei's love for books can be said to be extraordinarily thorough in its protection. However, this method, while good, is not something that a poor young man can do. It is like looking at the "Siku Quanshu" that is not for sale, with nothing to do but admire it. Speaking of the "Siku Quanshu," I think of the copy in Shenyang. In order to prevent loss, four copies were specifically written and placed in four different places, equivalent to Liu Shaomei's "three boats" plan. However, Liu Shaomei's books eventually went from three to two, and among the "Siku Quanshu," only the "Wenlan Pavilion" copy in Hangzhou is the most complete. If the "Wenlan Pavilion" copy were to... what would happen? I think there is no problem, because it is already being prepared again. The "Siku Quanshu" is being reprinted, and it is clearly stated in the origin of the printing that the number of copies will be increased from four to one thousand. What does it matter if one or two more copies are moved away? China has plenty of places and plenty of books. It has always been "happy to do good and not refuse anyone."

Seventeen

Wen Ting Shi’s “Wen Chen Ou Ji” contains many historical materials about the Taiwan campaign. Among them is a saying:

"After the peace talks were concluded, someone wrote a couplet on the city gate:

May the Emperor live ten thousand years without end, may all under heaven rejoice:

The three armies were defeated, the land was ceded to sue for peace.

Then another couplet was spread:

Taiwan Province has returned to Japan,

Yiheyuan is erecting stages once again."

The indignation of the people at that time and the imperial family's joy are evident here.

Two Brothers (6)(7) 245

— Written by Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

He spoke in a short, choppy, almost incoherent way, like someone suffering from hallucinations.

He seemed to have forgotten Jean and his mother in the next room. He spoke as if no one else was there, because he had to speak, because he was in so much pain, because he had pressed too hard on his wound. The wound swelled into a tumor, and the tumor burst, spewing pus that defiled everyone. He paced back and forth as usual, staring straight ahead, gesticulating, speaking in a kind of desperate madness; his throat was filled with sobs, a reaction of resentment towards himself; he confessed his suffering, that kind of family suffering, as if throwing his pain into the unheeding air filled with leaping words.

Jean was horrified, his eyes almost suddenly persuaded by his brother's blind force, he stood close to a door, guessing that their mother was listening behind that door.

She couldn't come out: she had to go through the living room to come out. But she hadn't returned to the living room; yet she didn't dare come in.

Pierre suddenly stamped his foot and shouted:

"Ah, I'm really a pig for saying these things!"

Then he ran downstairs without even putting on his hat.

The big door leading to the street slammed shut, the sound shocking Jean out of his deep stupor. Several seconds, which seemed longer than a few hours, passed, and his soul had not yet escaped from that state of blank foolishness. He felt that he had to consider things immediately, that he had to do something, but he waited, because of fear, weakness, and cowardice, he didn't even want to understand, to comprehend, to remember. He belonged to that kind of procrastinator who puts everything off until tomorrow, and even when he had to make a decision immediately, he still instinctively tried to delay for a while.

But after Pierre's shout, now the deep silence around him, the silence reflected from the walls and furniture, combined with the light of ten candles and two lamps, made him suddenly so terrified that he wanted to run away himself.

So he shook his thoughts, shook his heart, and tried to think.

He had never encountered any difficulties in his life. He was one of those people who drifted along, letting himself flow like water. He had studied diligently in elementary and secondary school to avoid being punished. He had completed his law studies at university in a regular and orderly manner, because his life was peaceful. Everything in the world seemed very natural to him, and did not attract his special attention. There was not a single secret place in his mind, because, due to his nature, he liked order and integrity. Therefore, he now faced this tragedy like someone who had never swam falling into the water.

He began to try to doubt. Had his brother lied because of resentment and jealousy?

But if he hadn't been desperate to the extreme, how could he have stooped to saying those insulting words about their mother? And in his ears, in his eyes, in their nerves, even in his flesh, there remained a part of Pierre's words, a part of the painful cries, some tones and gestures of pain that were as irresistible and undeniable as facts.

His spirit was completely shattered, he simply couldn't make a movement or have a will. He was in unbearable distress; and he felt that his mother was right behind the door, she had heard everything, she was waiting.

What was she doing? Not a single movement, a single tremor, a single breath, a single sigh, could make one think that there was a person behind the door panel. Had she run away? But where could she run away from? What if she had run away... what if she had jumped from the window to the street!

Grain: Flour and Wheat Futures Weakened, Then Rebounded 259

After the flour market opened in the morning, prices for all months showed an initial decline followed by a rebound. Because the quoted price of foreign wheat from Chicago fell by a small two or three jiao, and from Canada by a small four fen, the sentiment was extremely sluggish at the opening. Prices for the current month and January fell to 2 yuan 1 jiao 2 fen, and February fell to 2 yuan 1 jiao 2 fen 2 li and a half, slightly less than the previous day by 1 fen or 1 fen and a half. Subsequently, because there were very few sellers, and factories made slight purchases for the current month, sentiment turned for the better, rebounding by one or two fen compared to the opening. When the afternoon market opened, the current month continued to rise due to slight purchases from factories, and the market was firm. Trading volume was low for all distant months, and the market was hovering. However, the Hakka buyers were weak, and bullish positions in the current month were closed out, causing prices to soften again. It is heard that another shipment of foreign wheat has arrived for factories, but sales are not picking up, and inventories are increasing, making it difficult to be optimistic about future prospects. As a result, the current month improved slightly by 2.5 li, January improved by 7.5 li, February remained unchanged, March improved by 2.5 li, April improved by 5 li, and May improved by 2.5 li.

After the wheat market opened in the morning, prices for all months continued to show a slight decline. Because the quoted price of foreign wheat from Chicago fell by a small two or three jiao, and from Canada by a small four fen, and the market had very few buyers, with no activity from outside customers, prices for January and February once entered customs at 4 yuan, January falling to 3 yuan 9 jiao 7 fen, and February falling to 3 yuan 9 jiao 9 fen. Subsequently, due to urgent short covering, prices rebounded slightly. When the afternoon market opened, prices were slightly better due to the steady trend in the flour market, but soon turned weak again. As a result, only March and April improved by 1 fen each, with no changes for the rest. In the current wheat market, due to the sharp drop in standards and the import of foreign wheat, it is difficult for merchants to reject the goods. Prices have fallen by five fen to one jiao. Yao Bay wheat is quoted at 4 yuan 5 fen, and Bengbu wheat at 3 yuan 9 jiao 7 fen, totaling 1,200 bags, handled by Huafeng Xinda.

As a result, prices fell by a small chi. At this point, Hakka merchants showed slightly more interest, buying over 2,000 bags. The inventories of thick japonica from various regions were still acceptable, but the surge in supply led to insufficient absorption, resulting in a weakening market. Market prices fell by about a jiao. Du Yang's sharp goods were generally lacking and flat, and the path for Yin Bian Yuan became slightly sluggish, leading to a stabilizing trend.

Hakka Xian Rice Sales in Fujian Lagging 261

The market remains weak

Yesterday, after Hakka Xian rice's price reduction and strong sales the day before, sentiment stabilized slightly, and the market was also active. Some customers, due to the activity in the market, were unwilling to sell at low prices, and insisted on limited prices yesterday, refusing to sell at lower prices. However, sales in the local street were sluggish due to the sluggish sales of Hakka rice, and they also remained on the sidelines. Fujian merchants, due to the serious situation, the economy was not loose, and temporarily there were no ship berths available, so they stopped continuing purchases. The cessation of sales in Fujian caused both sentiment and the market to trend downward. Yesterday, the entire city only sold 163 bags of Wuhu Ji Yuan rice at 7 yuan 5 jiao 8 fen and 300 bags of Hunan Ji Bo rice at 7 yuan 2 jiao to 7 yuan 1 jiao 2 fen. The prices were similar to the previous market, it is said.

Soybeans Fell Another Four or Five Fen 262

Yesterday, although the outflow of soybeans was slightly more active, prices were declining. High-quality soybeans were flat due to scarcity, but medium-quality soybeans were subject to cheap sales. Factories adhered to the principle of only buying cheap goods. Seeing that merchants were willing to sell cheaply, they also took the opportunity to buy small quantities, leading to a continued decline of four or five fen in the market. Fortunately, the supply was not surging, so the decline was relatively moderate. Yesterday, the total market transaction volume for various soybeans was about eight or nine cartloads, it is said.

Dried and Sundry Goods: Sichuan Pickled Mustard Tuber Market Resumes Firmness 264

Piece Goods: Plain Serge Sales Decline 265

Plain serge always has business at the end of the year, and it is known as a popular item in the industry. Regular colors are even more popular, and there has been no decline in recent years. Currently, the trend of serge in the original color, regular blue, gray, and gray is seen to be downstream, especially the 3 yuan grade, which is even more in decline. Although both overt and covert prices have fallen, sales are still extremely sluggish. The reason is mostly due to the influence of the strong arrival of Japanese goods, coupled with the cold weather, the thin quality of serge, and buyers choosing other types of wool fabrics instead. Yesterday, only thirty to forty pieces were opened in the city at the association, and the price was cheaper than last week. Because it is not far from the end of the year, each store wants to sell goods and exchange them for cash.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talks

On Foot Binding 284

— Wei Ba

As the Republic of China is about to enter its 23rd year, discussing foot binding seems somewhat outdated; however, it is not. In recent days, orders concerning "small feet" have been repeatedly issued in the newspapers. First, Liu Jianqun, Director of the Political Training Department of the Peiping Military Branch, stated that foreigners were taking pictures of foot-bound women in villages near Zhangjiakou without the permission of the local government, creating malicious propaganda that "concerns the national image." This was submitted to the National Government and has been communicated to the主管 governments of all provinces by the Civil Service Department, instructing military and police agencies in all localities to strictly investigate and prohibit this practice. (See a Shanghai newspaper from the 11th of this month.) Furthermore, Li Shuchun and He Siyuan, inspectors from the Shandong Provincial Government, inspected Xiajin, Wucheng, Gaotang, Boping, and surrounding areas. They observed that the practice of foot binding among women was still prevalent in the counties they passed through. They sent a telegram to the provincial government requesting that all counties be notified to instruct officials of all agencies to actively promote foot release and to order students to wear armbands stating "Do not marry women with bound feet." (See a Tianjin newspaper from the 12th of this month.) "Based on this," the writing of "On Foot Binding" still seems quite novel.

Originally, binding a perfectly good pair of feet into "three-inch golden lotuses," causing women to sway and stagger while walking as if about to fall in the wind, was a unique indulgence of a particular ethnic group and not worthy of emulation. However, seeing these women ruin their bodies and injure themselves in the bitter effort to "please their admirers" paints a perfect picture of inequality between the sexes. The reason for this inequality lies in the economic background. Women in the past! Even now! Clearly, they have no economic standing. Since they have no control over the economy, they are naturally controlled by men who have economic power—this is an inevitable logic. Therefore, their only task is to please their admirers. They search through the collections of erotic poets for inspiration, destroying their "lotus boats" and creating "golden lotuses" and "crescent moons" for the ruling-class men to enjoy and praise as toys. The situation is truly pathetic. This concept seems to have become deeply ingrained in the minds of some.

Since the introduction of Western culture, enlightened women have risen to demand gender equality, and the "natural foot movement" was once all the rage. However, the result has been that, except for a few emancipated women in the cities, women in poor and remote areas—especially those north of the Yangtze River!—are, as the Shandong provincial inspectors reported, still widely practicing "foot binding." But what about the so-called emancipated women in the cities? They have merely changed from "three-inch golden lotuses" to "three-inch high heels," still "swaying and staggering" as they walk, "as if about to fall in the wind." This situation is somewhat similar to the political reforms of the past twenty years! Thus, although it appears on the surface that they have been liberated, they have merely replaced the old chains with new shackles. In reality, they are still living under the belief of "pleasing their admirers." Using beauty to flaunt oneself is the pitiable state of most women, displaying their weaknesses to others. Therefore, fashionable women who wear high heels should not mock their foot-bound peers, as they are essentially in the same situation, living a life of begging for mercy in a male-dominated society. In this regard, the Shandong provincial inspectors' observation is correct: ordering students to wear armbands stating "Do not marry women with bound feet" will, I believe, be effective. Similarly, if an order were issued stating "Do not marry women who wear high heels," I believe it could also make high heels disappear—or at least reduce their prevalence. Women's fear lies not in the criminal code, but in disagreements with men—or rather, with economic power. But that is where the tragedy lies. Banning foot binding leads to wearing high heels; if high heels are banned, new tricks to please men will arise to replace them. Until the economic status of women is effectively improved, this cannot be stopped, and there is no way to talk about "gender equality."

This is again a question of "human nature."

As for prohibiting foreigners from taking "small feet" pictures, this is originally intended to prevent washing dirty linen in public. However, it is impossible to prohibit outsiders before prohibiting insiders. A body full of sores will always have one or two exposed for others to see. What "concerns the national image" is surely not just "small feet"!

Page 21

French Novelist "De Gopailla" Enamored with Chinese Women 285

— Bing Ding

French luxury and prosperity are world-renowned; hence, its capital, Paris, is also called the "City of Flowers." The extravagance and flirtatiousness of French women are also world-renowned; therefore, most of the sensual, debauched, and erotic films depict French women. Students from our country often like to marry French women because they are intoxicated by their coquettishness and infatuated with their beauty. Who would want a "yellow-faced woman" who is made in China?

Little did we know that things would be different. A few days ago, the French novelist Mr. De Gopailla came to Peiping. He made a statement expressing great admiration for Chinese women, which was truly laughable. Ms. Pan Junying, a writer of the New Romantic School, expressed her opposition and refuted him point by point. Here is a record of what they said:

De Gopailla said: "My special impression of China is that the modern Chinese women are indescribably beautiful. The clothes they wear seem to be wrapped around their bodies, and their faces are flat."

Ms. Pan retorted: "In fact, French women wear clothes that are wrapped around their bodies. Chinese women are known for their propriety and cannot be subjected to the irresponsible slander of those who do not understand propriety!"

De Gopailla said: "My ideal person to marry is a humorous Chinese woman with 'Oriental beauty,' which would be a comfort for life."

Ms. Pan retorted: "This statement is even more outrageous: French youths fall in love, and Chinese youths also fall in love. How can one talk about marriage without falling in love?"

De Gopailla said: "The most beautiful Chinese women are in Suzhou. When I listened to Chinese songs at the Confucius Temple in Nanjing, there was a Suzhou singer named Xue Yanqin. Her graceful posture on stage captivated my soul for days."

Ms. Pan retorted: "Mr. De has not traveled in China for long, but he is already so absurd as to regard the singer Xue Yanqin as the representative of Suzhou women. May I ask how many Suzhou women Mr. De has seen and whether he has had long conversations with noble Suzhou women? Educated women in China deeply know that women are independent individuals; they are not exclusively engaged in social interactions and neglect their proper occupations. Why does Mr. De not observe this and instead slander and ridicule Chinese women? Chinese women consider Mr. De a 'literary rogue'!"

Haha! Hearing the words of this French novelist, Mr. De Gopailla, I couldn't help but laugh so hard that my teeth fell out. Ms. Pan Junying's rebuttal can be described as incisive and enlightening. After hearing it, Mr. De Gopailla can also understand the "dignity" of Chinese women. Mr. De said, "The clothes worn by modern Chinese women seem to be wrapped around their bodies." In fact, women in your country expose their breasts and show off their legs, and the beauty of their curves is indescribable. The art of the buttocks, in particular, is something that our country's women cannot learn even a fraction of. Women in your country are truly indescribably beautiful啊. Indeed, your French women have high noses, yellow hair, and yellow eyes: doesn't your old sir think that these are "beautiful elements"? However, weight can be measured, length can be determined, and quantity can be counted—all with specific tools and standards. Only "beauty" and "ugliness" lack measuring tools. A male dog finds a female dog more and more adorable the more he looks at her; a yellow bull finds another yellow bull more and more beautiful the more he looks at him. Birds of a feather flock together, so why should you look at the flat faces of our country's women and become a "lecher"?

It is said that "the standard beauty in the West is Caucasian; the standard beauty in the East is Suzhou." Beautiful mountains and rivers, the concentration of spiritual energy—is this the reason for the birth of beauties? In fact, it is not entirely so. Chinese prostitutes are divided into two gangs, "Suzhou" and "Yangzhou," with Suzhou being superior and Yangzhou being inferior. In fact, Suzhou is not a place that produces prostitutes. The area at the junction of Suzhou and Wuxi, called "Dangkou," is the special origin of prostitutes: people of the world should not wrong the people of Suzhou ah. Yangzhou prostitutes are ranked lower because their accent is not as fluent and gentle as that of Suzhou people. In fact, was not Xi Shi, whose beauty has been famous for thousands of years, from Shaoxing? She probably couldn't speak "Wu soft words." Mr. De Gopailla, seeing the Suzhou singer Xue Yanqin, was captivated for days. I wonder what his soul would be like if he met a Suzhou woman plowing the fields barefoot?

Dying to Please 286

— Dong Lin

In China, when a person dies, his or her relatives, acquaintances, or friends, regardless of whether they had any feelings for the deceased during his or her lifetime or even interacted much with him or her, always send some wreaths, tin foil, or incense candles...etc., because they feel that this is an unavoidable "etiquette." Whether it is beneficial to the deceased is another question.

Generally, people feel that these "gifts" are too meaningless, so some have advocated replacing these pointless "gifts" with tangible money to be used as a scholarship fund for the deceased. And in fact, this method has been implemented to a considerable extent. This, although it can make the deceased "leave a name for posterity," is still questionable whether it is beneficial to the deceased himself. The only ones who benefit are those poor students.

So how can the deceased actually benefit? This is a question that has long wanted to be solved but cannot be solved (?)

But we great Chinese, after all, are not as good as the "blue-eyed, blond-haired" foreigners, who solved this serious question (?) without much effort! If you don't believe it, look at the London correspondence of the World Society published in this newspaper on the 16th:

"The Daily Express published a strange advertisement, signed by Mr. Fairtham, which reads; 'To all my friends and enemies, the advertiser wishes that those who would give me gifts of fresh flowers and wreaths after my death would convert them into cash now, because this is much more beneficial than offering me withered flowers after death. Whether the donation is large or small, I will gratefully accept it. Fairtham, at the Storent Hotel.'"

Whether this foreign man is humorous or sad, we will not go into it, but we cannot help but wonder whether this plan (?) has any possibility of being implemented. Most people send those pointless "gifts" to the deceased merely driven by false etiquette, while that foreign man wants to obtain cash before his death, which inevitably makes one doubt its feasibility.

So, will this serious question (?) forever have no hope of being solved?

"Old" Talk 287

— Ze Qing

Generally, people are reluctant to consider themselves "old." Sometimes, when asked about their age, they always conceal at least three to five years or one to two years. Especially women, simply refuse to tell others their true age. As the saying goes, "Eighteen years old every year." This captures the psychology of many women, and the older people get, the more flirtatious they become. Look at Lao Lai Zi in the Spring and Autumn period, who still wore colorful clothes and played children's games even at the age of seventy. Although this was for entertainment purposes, later generations praised him as a model of filial piety. It is also an example of "old people not having old hearts." And look at the general women in society, pretending to be delicate and artificial, so-called "Xu Niang half-old, charm still remains." Isn't this evidence that old people have flirtatious hearts?

There are also several epithets that people absolutely refuse to accept. For example, calling a gluttonous person "old glutton" or "old greedy." Calling a useless person "old朽." Calling a confused person "old悖." Calling a stingy person "old慳." Calling an old and weak person "old邁," "old物!" or "old槍." Calling a pedantic person "old顽固." Calling a person who has lost virtue "old but not dead." If they receive such epithets, they not only refuse to accept them, but also desperately negotiate with the person who said them.

However, there are several epithets that both old and young people are happy to receive. For example, calling a teacher "old scholar" or "teacher." Calling a person with some reputation in the local area "old gentleman" or "old丈." If he himself or his children and grandchildren become officials, calling him "old爺," "old大人," "old太爺," or "old封翁," and calling his "wife" "old夫人" or "old太太." If he has a child at an old age, calling him "old蚌珠." Calling a person with ambitions at an old age "old骥伏枥." Calling a person with accomplishments at an old age "old少年." Calling a person with deep experience "old成练达," "old马识途." Calling a person who is familiar with handling affairs "old手." Calling a person with extraordinary air "old气横秋." Calling a person who is thoughtful "old谋深算." Calling a person who is sincere "old实君子." Sometimes he himself is happy and actually calls himself "old夫," "old汉," or "old手." If he is humble, he calls himself "old拙" or "old朽." Women mostly call themselves "old身." But there are also those who frankly call themselves "old娘." Monks call themselves "old衲." As for nuns... I don't know what they call themselves "old"!

When celebrating a birthday, whether it is thirty, forty, fifty, sixty... his own hopes and the praises of others are always the "older" the better. For example: wishing a man a long life "南極" "old"人." Wishing a couple a long life "齊眉偕老" "白頭偕老." In general, the hearts of adults and gentlemen not only want to be "older" but also hope to welcome old age as soon as possible. Therefore, they celebrate their birthdays every year. Some even celebrate their birthdays several times a year. It can be seen that the word "old" also gives people extremely joyful moments!

In addition, meritorious veterans are called "founding elders," and virtuous elders are called "耆老." Old servants are called "old家人." Old women are called "old太婆." Long-aged wine is called "old酒." Calling male cousins "old表." Calling close friends "old友." Calling elders "old伯." Calling paternal grand-uncles or elders "old公公." Calling shopkeepers "old闆." Calling fellow villagers "old乡." Calling prostitutes "old鸨." In Shanghai dialect, there are "old举," "old蟹," "old牌," "old前辈," "old资格," "大好old," "大老官"... There is also "出old" for scolding people, and "old土" for addiction.

The above is just what I can think of at the moment. As for the rest, I am too "old" to think of it all at once. When we use the word "old" for people, we need to consider it carefully. Never "rely on the old to sell the old" or "old三old四." Otherwise, it is easy to make people "old羞成怒" and give you a "old拳" while asking you, "Are you old or not"!

Modern Calligraphy and Paintings by Celebrities 288

— Chuan Shaoyan, courtesy name Meigen, pseudonym Dongchi Jushi from Hunan

In the Yu Gong, Qingzhou is said to have strange rocks that resemble aluminum. One calls them "strange stones," and those that resemble jade are now often found on the Qi'an River. These beautiful stones are indistinguishable from jade, and are mostly red, yellow, and white in color. Their patterns resemble the whorls on human fingers, being exquisitely clear and lovable. Even the most skilled artists cannot match them in their deliberate paintings. Could this be what the ancients referred to as "strange stones?" The beauty and ugliness of all things arise from comparison. I do not know where the truth lies. Written before the winter solstice of Guiyou year. Dongchi Yan

Page 23

Big Sale 289

— Zu

All the major companies, as well as the small shops, have "Spring Big Sales" in spring, "Summer Big Sales" in summer, autumn similarly has autumn big sales, and inevitably "Winter Big Sales" in winter. Besides these seasonal big sales, there are also so-called "Christmas Big Sales," "Special Big Sales," and "Closing Down Big Sales," etc. It seems that they cannot increase customers to buy their goods without "sales." Because of this, the "big sales" of these companies and small shops cannot help but arouse my great suspicion. I think: if their "sales" throughout the year really reduced prices, then these stores would close down at most after a year! Otherwise, this proves that their so-called "sales" are just a deceptive smokescreen.

My mother is most fond of chanting scriptures. She often says: "If I could have three copies of the Amitabha Sutra, two copies of the Lotus Sutra, and two copies of the Diamond Sutra, then I would die content. But to buy these sutras would cost several hundred yuan! "One day, a monk came to my house and said that when he was "in seclusion," he had chanted four copies of the Amitabha Sutra, three copies of the Lotus Sutra, and three copies of the Diamond Sutra. Now, because he wants to build a new temple, he is willing to bear the pain of "selling at a reduced price." Originally, the Diamond Sutra cost sixty yuan per copy, the Lotus Sutra forty yuan, and the Amitabha Sutra twenty-five yuan. Now they are all "discounted" by ten yuan. My mother was very happy to hear this and bought several copies of each from him. Ah! Even those who cultivate themselves with pure hearts have "big sale" days, so no wonder big sales are so common.

One day, I went to a school to play and saw a notice that said something like this: "From next week to Saturday will be the registration date for this school. If you register within the specified date, you can get a reduction of one-fifth of the tuition fee for the next semester. If you register after this period, you must pay all fees according to the regulations. If there are sisters registering together, the tuition fee can be discounted by 5%," and so on. This so-called "school" is also having a "big sale"!

In our hometown, some families treat their daughters like commodities. If the daughter is even slightly beautiful, they really treat her as a piece of property. Therefore, in terms of jewelry and betrothal gifts, they will use exploitative means to make demands on the "groom's family." But when the war broke out in Shanghai last year, and it was said that the countryside would also be affected, they couldn't afford the heavy burden of carrying young women, so when they met a suitable family, they sold their "property" at a discount丨betrothed丨them. "Big sales" have even come to marriage.

In this day and age, in this society, the "big sales" are probably not just the one or two things recorded here. Everything is subject to the fate of "big sales": things are like this, lives are like this, maps and territories are also like this! It's really not surprising.

Controversy Regarding the Term "My ××" 290

— Jingxin

Recently, I often see that anything used or eaten by children is prefixed with the word "my" as a name. For example, "My Pictorial" in a spring store, "My Pills" in a pharmacy, and so on. When I see these special and fashionable terms, I always have a big doubt: "What is this based on? Is it beneficial or harmful to children?" One day I questioned a friend about my doubts. He thought that "It only arouses children's interest or attention, and there is no question of benefit or harm." This answer cannot dispel my doubts. I feel that this question is small, but it has a great relationship with children.

According to Morgan's research on "Ancient Society," in the languages of primitive people and the barbarians still remaining on earth, there is no existence of "you" and "I," only "we," "you," and "them." The concept of "mine" came about after the emergence of the private property system. But when it comes to the future society, the relationship between people will inevitably become more complex and closer, groups will increase and occupy importance, and human life will gradually break away from the category of individualistic life and expand into collective life and social life. The concepts of "mine" and "individual" in the Middle Ages, when human beings were intoxicated and dominated by religion, feudal lords, and monarchs, did promote new social concepts. The prosperity of the early capitalist world was indeed the sole masterpiece of individualism. However, now that capitalism has developed to its final form, exposing unavoidable contradictions, society is suffering from panic, crisis, recession, overpopulation, overproduction, and other diseases. Individualism, which rose and fell with capitalism, will naturally end its mission like the setting sun near the Western Hills. If at this time someone still promotes individualism (just like advocating feudal warlords), everyone will boo it as an act of turning back the clock. In other words, desperately engraving the selfish concepts of "mine" and "own" on the pure and tender minds of children, and cultivating a person who only knows about himself and does not know about others, let alone the country or society, is this what society needs now or in the future? On the contrary, we should instill in children the concepts of society, country, and labor, and create producers who will be beneficial to society and useful to the country.

As for the word "mine," if it can arouse children's interest and attention, it is not the ultimate truth. Based on our usual observations, we know that children's psychology is similar to that of primitive people. They are thorough socialists who do not distinguish between you and me. Children often give their own things to their little friends without hesitation, and often take things from other people's homes that they think are useful without thinking it is stealing. We should make good use of this respectable foundation of children and make appropriate corrections. If we see a child grabbing other people's things without permission, instead of scaring him with the word "stealing," it would be better to persuade him with "Don't take things that others have worked hard to obtain, but create or exchange for things with your own hard work." This would be more effective and easier to understand.

In short, the current or future society definitely does not need people like warlords and treacherous merchants to dominate. I hope that the masters of the future - children - will be less infected with the germs of individualism left over from the old era.

▲ Invention of Skin-Moisturizing "Smooth" Water Dr. Xi Shitai has recently invented a skin-moisturizing water called "Smooth." It is a liquid, does not contain powder, and is non-sticky. It dries immediately upon application and has no pungent fragrance. When applied to the face, hands, and feet, it can make dry, rough, and chapped skin smooth and glossy. It can also eliminate frostbite before it ulcerates and reduce redness and itching. Men can apply it before and after shaving to prevent the occurrence of small rashes and eliminate the unpleasantness of the blade. Women can apply it before applying powder to make the powder extra smooth and delicate. Therefore, it can be used by men, women, and children of all ages, and is better than cold cream and honey. It is currently entrusted to the French Pharmacy as the general agent, with large bottles selling for five jiao and small bottles for three jiao.

Novel

Shanghai (II) (6) 292

— Zhang Laosan

(III) (8) Gloomy Dusk

To capture a woman's heart is not an easy task, but to win back a woman's heart is even more difficult. Sister Min is determined to leave, and I no longer have the ability to keep her. In a gloomy dusk, gloomy emotions climbed onto everyone's gloomy hearts. The entire Zhengyi Society's atmosphere was even more serious than when it was first sealed. Sister Min buried her head and took care of packing her belongings, not answering everyone's advice. Countless pairs of eyes moved up and down, left and right, following her hands, as if everyone's fate was controlled by those hands.

The wind blew across the roof, and everyone's breathing could be heard in the room.

"Miss Sun," a rough voice suddenly broke the gloomy atmosphere. Xiao Huang did not know when he was holding a package and standing at the door, saying: "From my own position, if I can't keep Miss Sun, I will leave here first." When he spoke, he no longer resembled the smiling fat man on the screen.

Sister Min looked back, and everyone looked back to watch the tragedy of the actor who was good at playing comedy leads.

Sister Min's eyes moved across everyone's faces. She understood everyone's urgent feelings. Like an oppressed person surrendering, she kicked the boxes and other things at her feet and sat heavily on the bed, saying helplessly, "I'm not leaving, I'm not leaving."

"Min, really?" Gao Fei said.

"You still don't trust me? I'm not that kind of person. I won't stab you in the back. I won't plot against anyone!"

I knew she was angry. I winked at Gao Fei.

"Min, I trust you. You are the soul of our society!"

"Miss Sun, I also trust you!" Xiao Huang threw the package in his hand on the floor at the door and raised his hand to give a military salute.

"Pfft:" Sister Min laughed.

A weight of a thousand catties was pushed away from everyone's gloomy hearts in this gloomy dusk.

"Go down, I'm not leaving. Let me rest for a while." Sister Min fell onto the bed, looking very tired.

No one said a word, and they quietly went down the three floors. A'Fu was poking his head at the stairs, and when he saw us coming downstairs, he asked stammeringly, "Mr. Gao, is it time for dinner?" His attitude was as if he was also carrying a bellyful of worries.

"Let's start. I'm really hungry." Gao Fei patted his belly through his clothes and sighed a long breath.

Xiao Huang sat on the sofa, still expressionless. I went over and patted him on the shoulder and said, "Xiao Huang, you saved me."

"I saved you?" He opened his eyes wide. "Or did I cause the disaster? If Miss Sun leaves today, I don't know how I would be able to face you and the Zhengyi Society."

I sighed and looked at the clock on the wall. It was five quarters of an hour later than the usual dinner time.
